{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:49:54","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:49:54","title":"Patching Distributed Cache for SharePoint 2013 and SharePoint 2016","link":"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/microsoft-sharepoint-blog/patching-distributed-cache-for-sharepoint-2013-and-sharepoint/ba-p/1562117","description":"<P>Is your SharePoint 2013 or 2016 farms Distributed Cache services Healthy? If not you might need to patch. One way to validate your Distributed Cache service is healthy is to pull some ULS logs from one of the Distributed cache servers in the farm.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Using <A href=\"http://www.microsoft.com/en-us/download/details.aspx?id=44020\" target=\"_self\">ULSViewer</A>, Filter your ULS log files where <STRONG>Category</STRONG> equals <STRONG>DistributedCache,&nbsp;</STRONG>if you see something like the screenshot below. Then your Distributed cache is not healthy and should patch your farm using the steps in this article.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>EventId Found -<FONT color=\"#FF0000\"> air4c, air4d, agyfw, air4c, air38, air39</FONT></STRONG></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"dc004.png\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/209904i454A58FF9F7E3BE9/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"dc004.png\" alt=\"dc004.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Steps for Patching Distributed cache</STRONG></P>\n<P>Patching the distributed cache service on your SharePoint farm will cause user experience to be interrupted a bit and its recommended to be performed during a maintenance window. But It can be performed during production if its all ready down in some cases.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Step 1 </STRONG>- Shut down the Distributed Cache service on one of the distributed cache servers in your farm.</P>\n<P>Run the following PowerShell command to stop the distributed cache on the server at a SharePoint command prompt.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\"><FONT color=\"#0000FF\"><STRONG>Stop-SPDistributedCacheServiceInstance -Graceful</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Step 2 </STRONG>- Patch AppFabric 1.1 on the one server you stopped the Distributed Cache service on.&nbsp;Patch the server with CU7 found in the following article where you can download it - <A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/kb/3092423\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/kb/3092423</A></P>\n<P><STRONG>&nbsp;</STRONG></P>\n<P><STRONG>Step 3</STRONG> - Update the “<STRONG>DistributedCacheService.exe.config</STRONG>” file to run garbage collection process in the background on each Distributed Cache server.&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT color=\"#800080\"><STRONG><FONT color=\"#000000\">File location</FONT> - C:\\Program Files\\AppFabric 1.1 for Windows Server\\DistributedCacheService.exe.config</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Update the file with the section below, see screen shot below – Make sure you put it in the right section or it will not work correctly.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-60px\"><FONT color=\"#0000FF\">&lt;appSettings&gt;</FONT></P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-60px\"><FONT color=\"#0000FF\">&nbsp;&nbsp; &lt;add key=\"backgroundGC\" value=\"true\"/&gt;</FONT></P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-60px\"><FONT color=\"#0000FF\">&lt;/appSettings&gt;</FONT></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"dc001.png\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/209892i8A2C1C8A1FA03A69/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"dc001.png\" alt=\"dc001.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Step 4 </STRONG>- Repeat steps <STRONG>1</STRONG> through <STRONG>3</STRONG> on the next distributed cache sever in the farm, repeat these steps until you have patched all the Distributed cache servers using these steps. Once you have them all patched, move on to Step <STRONG>5</STRONG>.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Step 5 - </STRONG>Fine-tune the Distributed Cache service by using a Windows PowerShell script found in this Microsoft article near the bottom in the section called:</P>\n<P>“<STRONG>Fine-tune the Distributed Cache service by using a Windows PowerShell script</STRONG>”</P>\n<P>&nbsp;<A href=\"https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/jj219613.aspx\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/jj219613.aspx</A></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Run the script found in the article on one of your SharePoint servers in the farm. This only has to be done once.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Note – there is a section for SharePoint 2013 and 2016 in the Microsoft article – Use the section that matches your farm.</STRONG></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-90px\"><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"dc003.png\" style=\"width: 390px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/209893i23C7EDE707EC26A4/image-size/medium?v=1.0&amp;px=400\" title=\"dc003.png\" alt=\"dc003.png\" /></span></P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-90px\">&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Step 6 </STRONG>- Start the Distributed cache service using the below PowerShell script in a SharePoint PowerShell command prompt on one of the Distributed cache servers.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\"><FONT color=\"#0000FF\"><STRONG>$instanceName =\"SPDistributedCacheService Name=AppFabricCachingService\"</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\"><FONT color=\"#0000FF\"><STRONG>$serviceInstance = Get-SPServiceInstance | ? {($_.service.tostring()) -eq $instanceName -and ($_.server.name) -eq $env:computername}</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\"><FONT color=\"#0000FF\"><STRONG>$serviceInstance.Provision()</STRONG><STRONG>&nbsp;</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Step 7 </STRONG>– Verify the health of the Distributed cache server you started in Step <STRONG>6</STRONG> using the below PowerShell commands, Do not go to Step <STRONG>8</STRONG> until the server shows UP. You might have to wait a bit for it to come up, its usually slow on the first server to start up.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\"><FONT color=\"#0000FF\"><STRONG>Use-CacheCluster</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\"><FONT color=\"#0000FF\"><STRONG>Get-CacheHost</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>NOTE -&nbsp;</STRONG>If you have servers listed as Down, try starting the Distributed cache service in Central admin and re-run the above commands to verify it came up.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;<STRONG>Step 8 – </STRONG>Repeat Step <STRONG>6</STRONG> through <STRONG>7</STRONG> on the rest of the Distributed cache servers until they are all started.&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;<STRONG>Step 9 – </STRONG>Once all the servers are up, check their health using the new Safari 13.1 browser with Intelligent Tracking Prevention (ITP), 3rd party cookies are not allowed by default to remove the ability for websites to track you using cookies.\n</P> \n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">\n When an iframe is hosted in a page, it's cookies, even if they are for the origin in the frame are considered 3rd party if it is hosted in a page that is a different origin. This causes the cookies set for the SharePoint add-in webpart model to not be sent on subsequent requests, including the authentication cookie (fedauth).\n</P> \n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">\n &nbsp;\n</P> \n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">\n <FONT size=\"4\">\n  <STRONG>\n   The Solution\n  </STRONG>\n </FONT>\n</P> \n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">\n There is a solution to this by adding some code to request access to these cookies via a storage access API that has been implemented in Safari, and Firefox, as well as browsers based on their respective projects (webkit and mozilla) and has experimental/future support in Chrome and Edge (chromium) as well.\n</P> \n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">\n &nbsp;\n</P> \n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">\n This script code will allow you to request 16:49:54","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:49:54","title":"Agile IT management of your SharePoint-powered intelligent intranet","link":"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/microsoft-sharepoint-blog/agile-it-management-of-your-sharepoint-powered-intelligent/ba-p/1604914","description":"<P>Business changes at a faster pace today more than ever before. The agility of IT to be both proactive and reactive in the face of change is a must. Adapt, or fade out. &nbsp;This affects everything and must be reflected in your intranet. The more change you can absorb and respond to, the more value you can provide without compromise or arduous task – for both change and growth expansion.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Microsoft has released numerous admin capabilities to both modernize your intranet, manage change, and keep it dynamic. The SharePoint admin center offers the flexibility and control you need to manage everything your intelligent intranet requires. SharePoint admins create and manage sites, establish or adjust the primary intranet entry point, optimize for spanning geographies – location and languages, and more.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<UL>\n<LI><STRONG>Adjust a SharePoint site address</STRONG></LI>\n<LI><STRONG>Update the root SharePoint site</STRONG></LI>\n<LI><STRONG>OneDrive and SharePoint multi-geo</STRONG></LI>\n<LI><STRONG>Support multiple languages across your intranet</STRONG></LI>\n</UL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"AgileIT_SP-admin-center.gif\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/213849i9FA580D8697356C5/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"AgileIT_SP-admin-center.gif\" alt=\"Cycling through several SharePoint admin center pages used to manage sites, optimize experiences across multiple regions, adjust sharing controls, plan and execute migrations, and more.\" /><span class=\"lia-inline-image-caption\" onclick=\"event.preventDefault();\">Cycling through several SharePoint admin center pages used to manage sites, optimize experiences across multiple regions, adjust sharing controls, plan and execute migrations, and more.</span></span></STRONG></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<H1>Adjust a SharePoint site address</H1>\n<P>Things change, often. Especially when something starts as a concept or a pilot, and then solidifies into a project or product. A SharePoint site with a codename in the URL is no longer the headache it once was.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>It is possible for SharePoint administrators to change site URLs. As a global or SharePoint admin, you will be able to change site URLs for the following types of SharePoint sites: classic team sites, communication sites, and both modern team sites that are Microsoft 365 Groups-connected and ones that don't belong to an Microsoft 365 Groups. And it is possible to perform this action from with the SharePoint admin center or via PowerShell.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"Change-site-address.jpg\" style=\"width: 342px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/213850i08F189B6EE001C99/image-size/medium?v=1.0&amp;px=400\" title=\"Change-site-address.jpg\" alt=\"Change the site URL by typing the new desired site address, seeing if it's available, and clicking OK.\" /><span class=\"lia-inline-image-caption\" onclick=\"event.preventDefault();\">Change the site URL by typing the new desired site address, seeing if it's available, and clicking OK.</span></span></P>\n<P>So, for example, if you have a site named:&nbsp;<A href=\"https://contoso.sharepoint.com/sites/Develpment\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://contoso.sharepoint.com/sites/Develpment</A>, you can rename the site to correct the incorrect spelling of \"development\" via the SharePoint admin center. And best of all, the service automatically-generates redirects to ensure that old links do not break.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Note: You can't change the domain (\"contoso\" in the previous example) or any other part of the path. For example, you can't move the site from \"/sites\" to \"/teams.\"</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>It’s inevitable that a site used for the early stages of a project or product in development to require adjust further along in the process – when final names and brands are decided, or simply when ownership changes.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Learn more about <A href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/sharepoint/change-site-address\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">changing a SharePoint site address in Microsoft 365</A>.&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<H1><SPAN>Update the root SharePoint site</SPAN></H1>\n<P>Your root site originally began as a classic, non-group connected SharePoint team site. And now you can make your root site one that is meant more for communication across the company – a modern communication site (recommended). And you, too, can swap in a modern team site if preferred.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Like a magician’s trick (that’s no longer secret), the power to invoke a SharePoint root site swap is possible. You can make your Contoso.Sharepoint.com site – your root site – much more meaningful with just a few clicks. Use the <STRONG>Replace site</STRONG> button in the admin center or via PowerShell using the new cmdlet: Invoke-SPOSiteSwap. Ta da! Rabbit out of the hat. Once swapped, the source site becomes the new SharePoint root site for your tenant. And the previously designated root site automatically gets archived along with any subsites that may have existed.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"Replace-root-site.jpg\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/213851iA77A31A05BC1FF7A/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"Replace-root-site.jpg\" alt=\"You can now swap the root site with the site of your choice directly from within the SharePoint admin center.\" /><span class=\"lia-inline-image-caption\" onclick=\"event.preventDefault();\">You can now swap the root site with the site of your choice directly from within the SharePoint admin center.</span></span></P>\n<P>Before and during the site swap, the source or target sites cannot be \"associated\" with an Office 365 group or be connected to a SharePoint hub site. If the site is \"associated\" to a Hub Site, then the association can be removed, the swap performed, and the Hub Site re-associated after performing the swap. And it may be that you wish the newly swapped in root site to be a hub site – which you can establish – after the swap.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Note: The <STRONG>Replace site</STRONG> button in the SharePoint admin center is currently only available for customers with less than 10,000 licenses. We will share more before the close of this year when it becomes available to customers of all sizes.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><A href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/powershell/module/sharepoint-online/invoke-spositeswap\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Learn more</A>.&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<H1>OneDrive and SharePoint multi-geo</H1>\n<P>Growth. Expansion. Desired outcomes, and a good sign for the business. IT is challenged to keep pace with acquisitions, cross-region movement of people and projects, and the expectation to deliver the best possible performance along with improved data residency across the company per country-by-country policy.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Multi-geo allows multinational companies to meet data residency obligations in M365 by expanding their existing tenant into our GoLocal and regional datacenters. Because Multi-Geo is a single tenant, users can collaborate as a single global organization with a seamless, unified experience.&nbsp; Multi-Geo is offered for OneDrive, SharePoint online, and Exchange online.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Administrators can assign where a user's OneDrive gets created through the user's preferred data location (PDL) attribute. Likewise, the user's PDL determines where they can create shared resources like SharePoint Sites and Groups. OneDrive sites and SharePoint sites can be moved across geo locations as data residency needs change.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Each user's OneDrive can be provisioned in or&nbsp;<A href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/office365/enterprise/move-onedrive-between-geo-locations\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">moved by an administrator</A>&nbsp;to a satellite location in accordance with the user's PDL. Personal files are then kept in that geo location, though they can be shared with users in other geo locations. And when a user creates a SharePoint group-connected site in a multi-geo environment, their PDL is used to determine the geo location where the site and its associated Group mailbox is created. (If the user's PDL value hasn't been set or has been set to geo location that hasn't been configured as a satellite location, then the site and mailbox are created in the central location).</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"Multi-geo.jpg\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/213852i8712042CF9A1094E/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"Multi-geo.jpg\" alt=\"Setting up and managing your multi-geo environment is done through the SharePoint admin center.\" /><span class=\"lia-inline-image-caption\" onclick=\"event.preventDefault();\">Setting up and managing your multi-geo environment is done through the SharePoint admin center.</span></span></P>\n<P>With more data residency measures being legislated around the world for cloud data, global businesses are challenged with meeting their data residency requirements and digitally transforming with the cloud.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Multi-Geo addresses these challenges by enabling a single Microsoft 365 tenant to span multiple regions and/or countries and giving customers the flexibility to choose the country or region where each employee’s Microsoft 365 data is stored at-rest. This helps businesses meet their global data residency needs and digitally transform with Microsoft 365.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Get the latest <A href=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/office-365-blog/multi-geo-reduced-seat-minimum-and-expanded-geo-coverage/ba-p/1310777\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">multi-geo updates</A>, plus review the <A href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/Office365/Enterprise/office-365-multi-geo\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Microsoft 365 multi-geo admin guide</A>.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<H1>Support multiple languages across your intranet</H1>\n<P>Language inside the intranet cannot be a barrier. Global organizations need to enable content across different languages and so we are delivering multilingual site capabilities. This will enable you to create content and sites in multiple languages. Customers can publish and consume modern SharePoint pages/news with language translations.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>The multilingual publishing feature for SharePoint communication sites, now rolled out worldwide, enables you to create and translate pages, set translator roles, and get email alerts when pages are ready to be translated, updated, and published. All of this comes on top of the rich and flexible pages and news creation experience in SharePoint.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"Multi-lingual.jpg\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/213853iA3D3E701014673D7/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"Multi-lingual.jpg\" alt=\"A SharePoint-based intranet can support multiple languages for important sites and pages meant to be consumed by multiple people from multiple regions. People can easily switch from one language to the other.\" /><span class=\"lia-inline-image-caption\" onclick=\"event.preventDefault();\">A SharePoint-based intranet can support multiple languages for important sites and pages meant to be consumed by multiple people from multiple regions. People can easily switch from one language to the other.</span></span></P>\n<P>Communication between teams, managers, and everyone in between is one of the most important things an organization can facilitate currently. With many teams spread all over the globe, Microsoft is proud to be able to provide a tool built into modern SharePoint that helps to ensure your information is easily delivered to your team. Get more information, exact steps and troubleshooting tips in our article:&nbsp;<A href=\"https://support.office.com/en-us/article/create-multilingual-communication-sites-pages-and-news-2bb7d610-5453-41c6-a0e8-6f40b3ed750c?ui=en-US&amp;rs=en-US&amp;ad=US\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Create multilingual communication sites, pages, and news</A>. You can also view a video demo of the feature&nbsp;<A href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=V3mtnoIlFEY\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">here</A>&nbsp;or hear more about the building of the feature in this&nbsp;<A href=\"http://intrazone.mpsn.libsynpro.com/sharepoint-roadmap-pitstop-march-2020\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Intrazone podcast.</A></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<H1>Try more of what SharePoint offers – additional resources</H1>\n<P>Harness the power of the intelligent intranet to communicate effectively across the organization, engage employees,&nbsp;and connect with relevant information and knowledge. our timeline and support for the retiring of SharePoint 2010 Workflows, how to access Visio as a tab within Teams channels, sharing of moved files, and more. Details &amp; screenshots below, including our audible companion: <STRONG>The</STRONG> <STRONG>Intrazone Roadmap Pitstop: August 2020</STRONG> podcast episode – all to help answer, \"What's rolling out now for SharePoint and related technologies into Microsoft 365?\"</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><IFRAME src=\"https://html5-player.libsyn.com/embed/episode/id/15815837/height/90/theme/custom/thumbnail/yes/direction/backward/render-playlist/no/custom-color/247bc1/\" width=\"100%\" height=\"90\" scrolling=\"no\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\" webkitallowfullscreen=\"webkitallowfullscreen\" style=\"border: none;\" mozallowfullscreen=\"mozallowfullscreen\" oallowfullscreen=\"\" msallowfullscreen=\"\"></IFRAME></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>In the podcast episode, I chat with <STRONG>Lincoln DeMaris </STRONG>(<A href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/lincoln-demaris-2950439/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">LinkedIn</A> | <A href=\"https://twitter.com/lincolnator\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Twitter</A>), principal program manager at Microsoft who works on Microsoft Lists. We talked about the state of the Lists roll out, how it evolves from what we know as SharePoint lists, some of the early feedback, and tackle some of the most common frequently asked questions about Microsoft Lists.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_001_Lincoln-DeMaris_profile.jpg\" style=\"width: 251px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/215631i5811B30213AF8791/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_001_Lincoln-DeMaris_profile.jpg\" alt=\"Lincoln DeMaris, principal program manager (Microsoft Lists / Microsoft) [Intrazone guest]\" /><span class=\"lia-inline-image-caption\" onclick=\"event.preventDefault();\">Lincoln DeMaris, principal program manager (Microsoft Lists / Microsoft) [Intrazone guest]</span></span></P>\n<P>All features listed below began rolling out to Targeted Release customers in Microsoft 365 as of August 2020 (possibly early September 2020).</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"5\"><STRONG>Inform and engage with dynamic employee experiences</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>Build your intelligent intranet on SharePoint in Microsoft 365 and get the benefits of investing in business outcomes – reducing IT and development costs, increasing business speed and agility, and up-leveling the dynamic, personalized, and welcoming nature of your intranet.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>SharePoint site templates for Education</STRONG></P>\n<P>These are for schools and universities, made available via the Microsoft&nbsp;<A href=\"https://lookbook.microsoft.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Look Book</A>. Each brings together news, events, highlighted content, quick links and more, pre-configured and designed with a specific scope and audience for a variety of Education scenarios.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_002_SP-EDU-templates.jpg\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/215632i33FE3A52B495F0EF/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_002_SP-EDU-templates.jpg\" alt=\"SharePoint site template: &quot;School home page&quot; - across several screen sizes.\" /><span class=\"lia-inline-image-caption\" onclick=\"event.preventDefault();\">SharePoint site template: \"School home page\" - across several screen sizes.</span></span></P>\n<P>Here is a quick highlight of each of the four templates: &nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<UL>\n<LI><A href=\"https://lookbook.microsoft.com/details/44dc3585-9140-4183-81fc-bdb057f71ac1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">School home page</A>: a central, institution-wide landing experience for students and staff to showcase the latest happenings and important resources.</LI>\n<LI><A href=\"https://lookbook.microsoft.com/details/eb5d4741-e2f4-44f1-954b-e7d598585c63\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Staff home page</A>: a dashboard for staff members with time-saving links, documents, and calls-to-action. It's designed to be used with a&nbsp;<A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/office/create-a-staff-team-in-microsoft-teams-314ac9d5-36a9-408e-8ae4-7ef20e9f1ddf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Staff team</A>&nbsp;or a&nbsp;<A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/office/create-a-plc-team-in-microsoft-teams-ad803fa2-c967-41b4-ae37-0bf60f17fa00\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Professional Learning Community (PLC) team</A>&nbsp;in *Microsoft Teams for Education*</LI>\n<LI><A href=\"https://lookbook.microsoft.com/details/f70a722f-e20a-4f0e-a0e7-ed75b3c9a74a\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Class home page</A>: this is a dashboard for a class with resources, updates, and learning content, and designed to be used with a&nbsp;<A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/office/create-a-class-team-in-microsoft-teams-fae422eb-58b7-4431-9ff2-a4b9b6ae7c5b\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Class team</A>&nbsp;in *Microsoft Teams for Education*</LI>\n<LI><A href=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/microsoft-sharepoint-blog/inform-and-engage-students-and-staff-with-sharepoint-site/ba-p/1557285\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Learn more</A>.</LI>\n</UL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Azure CDN caching for SharePoint and OneDrive video</STRONG></P>\n<P>We are pleased to introduce improved support for videos; aka, better streaming performance for videos you store in SharePoint and OneDrive.&nbsp;Videos that are accesses often will be streamed from the Azure CDN closest to the user to optimize the playback experience. At all times data will remain within the Microsoft 365 compliance boundary.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>This is a great area for growth that also paves the way for future innovation. Stay tuned to this space.</P>\n<UL>\n<LI>Roadmap ID:&nbsp;<A href=\"https://www.microsoft.com/microsoft-365/roadmap?filters=&amp;searchterms=66065\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">66065</A>.&nbsp;</LI>\n<LI><A href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/office365/enterprise/content-delivery-networks\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Learn more about CDNs</A></LI>\n</UL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Retiring SharePoint 2010 Workflows</STRONG></P>\n<P>Since the release of SharePoint workflows, Microsoft has evolved workflow orchestration to not only encompass SharePoint, but all the productivity services you use with Microsoft 365 and beyond. With the continued investment in Power Automate as the universal solution to workflow, Microsoft is retiring SharePoint 2010 workflows. We recommend customers to move to Power Automate or other supported solutions.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Timeline:</P>\n<UL>\n<LI>Starting August 1st, 2020, SharePoint 2010 workflows will be turned off for any newly created tenants.</LI>\n<LI>Starting November 1st, 2020, Microsoft will remove the ability to run, or create, and or execute SharePoint 2010 workflows from existing tenants.</LI>\n</UL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_003_SP-2010-workflows-to-PowerAutomate.jpg\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/215633iA2BFAF5519C1C94A/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_003_SP-2010-workflows-to-PowerAutomate.jpg\" alt=\"Planning to move from classic SharePoint Workflows to Power Automate flows.\" /><span class=\"lia-inline-image-caption\" onclick=\"event.preventDefault();\">Planning to move from classic SharePoint Workflows to Power Automate flows.</span></span></P>\n<P>Note: SharePoint 2013 workflows remain supported, although turned off by default for new tenants starting November 1st, 2020.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Resources:&nbsp;&nbsp;</P>\n<UL>\n<LI>Use the&nbsp;<A href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/sharepoint/dev/transform/modernize-scanner\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">SharePoint Modernization Scanner</A>&nbsp;tool to scan your tenants for legacy workflow usage.&nbsp;</LI>\n<LI>Review the guidance for&nbsp;<A href=\"https://aka.ms/sp-workflows-guidance\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">migrating from classic workflows to Power Automate resources.&nbsp;&nbsp;</LI>\n<LI>Related to Microsoft 365 admin center message post #MC217999.</LI>\n</UL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Download SharePoint site usage data in Excel</STRONG></P>\n<P>Site owners, from the Site usage page, will be able to export their site's 90-day usage data in an Excel report. You can then build out a process that works for you per your preferences or governance requirements, to download the data on a recurring basis and build out the analysis you desire in Excel, or take it beyond and visualize the data in Power BI.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_004_Export-site-usage.jpg\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/215634i3731EC2A91BFDF65/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_004_Export-site-usage.jpg\" alt=\"View information about how users interact with your site. SharePoint is the intelligent content service that powers teamwork – to better collaborate on proposals, projects, and campaigns throughout your organization – with integration across Microsoft Teams, OneDrive, Yammer, Stream, Planner and much more.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Updating the list and list item sharing experience</STRONG></P>\n<P>Site owners, members and visitors will now see a Share command when they are viewing a list, even when they do not have any list item selected. Site owners will be able to grant other users access to the list and can specify whether to give View-only, Edit, or Full Control permissions to the list. Other users (e.g. site members and visitors) cannot directly grant other users access to the list, but they can use the dialog to send an approval request to site owners if the site is set up to allow access requests (enabled by default).</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_005_Share-list-list-items.jpg\" style=\"width: 252px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/215635i0567883DA0C68B29/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_005_Share-list-list-items.jpg\" alt=\"Sharing lists and list items, so that you can decide whether to let people edit or just view them, and whether the people you share with can share with others.\" /><span class=\"lia-inline-image-caption\" onclick=\"event.preventDefault();\">Sharing lists and list items, so that you can decide whether to let people edit or just view them, and whether the people you share with can share with others.</span></span></P>\n<P>This update also brings sharing links to list items. When users select a list item and click Share, they will see the same Send Link sharing dialog that exists today with new options. Specifically, the “People in your organization with the link” and “Anyone with the link” options will be available based on the policy that your organization has configured.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>All the sharing policies you have configured for files will apply to list items. For example, if you have set “People in your organization with the link” as the default link type then that will also apply to list items. Similarly, if you have disabled or restricted \"Anyone links\" then those will also be disabled or restricted when users are sharing list items.</P>\n<UL>\n<LI>Roadmap ID:&nbsp;<A href=\"https://www.microsoft.com/microsoft-365/roadmap?filters=&amp;searchterms=64164\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">64164</A>.</LI>\n<LI><STRONG>Learn more:</STRONG>&nbsp;<A href=\"https://support.office.com/article/share-lists-and-list-items-in-sharepoint-3af7efa5-c7fd-4239-b704-7dc3a3f8e508\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Share lists and list items in SharePoint</A></LI>\n</UL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>SharePoint lists and libraries - improved image columns</STRONG></P>\n<P>It is much easier now to work with images in lists and libraries. Once an Image column is added to a list or library, users can add an image using the list or library form. They, too, can view, replace, or remove the image when viewing the item or file properties in the form. When users are browsing the list on a mobile device, they will be able to upload an image - including taking a photo with the device's camera.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_006_Image-column.jpg\" style=\"width: 400px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/215636iB8F2EB311FF13F32/image-size/medium?v=1.0&amp;px=400\" title=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_006_Image-column.jpg\" alt=\"Add an image to a list items using the improved Image column capabilities.\" /><span class=\"lia-inline-image-caption\" onclick=\"event.preventDefault();\">Add an image to a list items using the improved Image column capabilities.</span></span></P>\n<UL>\n<LI>Learn more:&nbsp;<A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/office/list-and-library-column-types-and-options-0d8ddb7b-7dc7-414d-a283-ee9dca891df7\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">List and library column types and options</A>.&nbsp;</LI>\n<LI>Roadmap ID:&nbsp;<A href=\"https://www.microsoft.com/microsoft-365/roadmap?filters=&amp;searchterms=64872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">64872</A>.</LI>\n</UL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Move files, and keep sharing</STRONG></P>\n<P>Collaboration requires the flow of work access to go unbroken. When you move a file to a new location in Microsoft 365, you will have the option to continue sharing the file from its new destination. A simple pop-up to confirm and keep moving forward.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_007_Move-file-continue-share.jpg\" style=\"width: 350px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/215637iDA66D5315361ED10/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_007_Move-file-continue-share.jpg\" alt=\"When you move a file to a new location in Microsoft 365, you will have the option to continue sharing the file from its new destination.\" /><span class=\"lia-inline-image-caption\" onclick=\"event.preventDefault();\">When you move a file to a new location in Microsoft 365, you will have the option to continue sharing the file from its new destination.</span></span></P>\n<P>The new link match permissions just like the source location and we send your collaborators an e-mail that notifies them that the file has been moved.</P>\n<P>Learn more:</P>\n<UL>\n<LI><A href=\"https://www.microsoft.com/microsoft-365/blog/2020/07/01/introducing-new-onedrive-features-to-share-and-collaborate-across-work-and-life/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Introducing new OneDrive features to share and collaborate across work and life</A></LI>\n<LI><A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/office/move-or-copy-files-in-sharepoint-00e2f483-4df3-46be-a861-1f5f0c1a87bc\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Move or copy files in SharePoint</A></LI>\n<LI><A href=\"https://www.microsoft.com/microsoft-365/blog/2020/07/01/introducing-new-onedrive-features-to-share-and-collaborate-across-work-and-life/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Move and keep sharing</A>&nbsp;is a new feature that allows your end users to easily re-share a file with all the direct collaborators (e.g., the users who had previously received a share for that file) should it be moved.</LI>\n<LI>Roadmap ID:&nbsp;<A href=\"https://www.microsoft.com/microsoft-365/roadmap?filters=&amp;searchterms=65907\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">65907</A>.&nbsp;</LI>\n</UL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"5\"><STRONG>Related technology</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P><STRONG>Yammer discovery feed </STRONG></P>\n<P>One superpower of Yammer is discovery – discovering new communities and new conversations that help broaden your perspective. This is the place for you to catch up on conversations happening in the communities you belong to.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_008_Yammer-discovery-feed.jpg\" style=\"width: 699px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/215638iC746D5AA9E1AC200/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_008_Yammer-discovery-feed.jpg\" alt=\"Use the Yammer discovery feed to discover new communities and new conversations.\" /><span class=\"lia-inline-image-caption\" onclick=\"event.preventDefault();\">Use the Yammer discovery feed to discover new communities and new conversations.</span></span></P>\n<P>Note for admins: you can select specific conversations to be *Featured Conversations* for a specific date. These conversations will be highlighted at the top of the Home Feed for everyone, until they have been read by the user or the time passes, and new content gets highlighted.</P>\n<UL>\n<LI><A href=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/yammer-blog/yammer-discovery-what-is-in-my-feed/ba-p/1596230\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Learn more</A>, plus new support article:&nbsp;<A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/office/what-s-in-the-yammer-home-feed-8fff52dd-5b38-468c-b963-fa4c6a4f9254\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">feed in Yammer</A>.</LI>\n<LI>Roadmap ID: <A href=\"https://www.microsoft.com/microsoft-365/roadmap?filters=&amp;searchterms=59319\" target=\"_self\">59319</A>.</LI>\n</UL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Access Visio directly from a tab within Teams channels</STRONG></P>\n<P>As part of our commitment to make collaborating on Visio diagrams within Teams seamless, we have added the ability to have “Visio as a tab.”&nbsp;This brings co-authoring on a diagram in real time.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_009_Visio-Teams.jpg\" style=\"width: 645px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/215639i08855B51854B4117/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_009_Visio-Teams.jpg\" alt=\"Visio tabs in Teams allow team members to access services and content in a dedicated space within a channel or in a chat.\" /><span class=\"lia-inline-image-caption\" onclick=\"event.preventDefault();\">Visio tabs in Teams allow team members to access services and content in a dedicated space within a channel or in a chat.</span></span></P>\n<P>You can keep important processes at your fingertips – like giving your sales team a way to visualize specific steps to solve customer questions and concerns. Or simplify brainstorming on business diagrams like SWOT analysis, Venn diagrams, pyramid diagrams.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<UL>\n<LI>Learn more: <A href=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/visio-blog/visio-as-a-tab-in-microsoft-teams-is-generally-available/ba-p/1474787\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Visio tabs in Teams</A>&nbsp;allow team members to quickly access content in a dedicated space within a channel or in a chat.</LI>\n<LI>Roadmap ID: <A href=\"https://www.microsoft.com/microsoft-365/roadmap?filters=&amp;searchterms=20886\" target=\"_self\">20886</A>.</LI>\n</UL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Microsoft 365 Network Connectivity Principles</STRONG></P>\n<P>Connectivity is one of the most critical decisions that customers should make to achieve best performance and delightful user experiences. We fine tune the Microsoft 365 for optimal features and connectivity, and there are several things you can do to optimize your network.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Microsoft has developed four *Network Connectivity* principles to help customers evaluate their existing network architectures and prepare or optimize readiness for Microsoft 365 - with security and privacy firmly intact.&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><LI-VIDEO vid=\"https://youtu.be/Kzf-NGaeIhc\" align=\"center\" size=\"large\" width=\"600\" height=\"338\" uploading=\"false\" thumbnail=\"https://i.ytimg.com/vi/Kzf-NGaeIhc/hqdefault.jpg\" external=\"url\"></LI-VIDEO></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>The 4 principles:</P>\n<OL>\n<LI><STRONG>Optimize Microsoft 365 traffic</STRONG> from our endpoint and differentiate it from generic Internet traffic for more efficient routing.</LI>\n<LI><STRONG>Enable local egress</STRONG> | Egress Microsoft 365 data connections through the Internet as close to your users as practical with matching DNS resolution.</LI>\n<LI><STRONG>Enable direct connectivity</STRONG> | Avoid network hairpins and minimize network latency to Microsoft’s global network.</LI>\n<LI><STRONG>Modernize security for SaaS</STRONG> | Avoid intrusive network security by bypassing proxies, traffic inspection devices, and avoid duplicating security controls already available in Microsoft 365.</LI>\n</OL>\n<UL>\n<LI><A href=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/microsoft-365-blog/microsoft-365-network-connectivity-principles/ba-p/1579560\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Learn more</A> + <A href=\"https://aka.ms/tune\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://aka.ms/tune</A> --&gt; \"Network planning and performance tuning for Microsoft 365\"</LI>\n</UL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>And last, did you see <STRONG>OneDrive on the Surface Duo</STRONG>?</P>\n<P>Panos Panay looking at photos in OneDrive: <A href=\"https://youtu.be/R1CNwBzYqRs?t=568\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://youtu.be/R1CNwBzYqRs?t=568</A> - spanning OneDrive on two screens and staying in the flow.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_010_OneDrive-on-Surface-Duo.jpg\" style=\"width: 620px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/215640i1323F7AE198279D1/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"IZ-RP-21_August-2020_022_010_OneDrive-on-Surface-Duo.jpg\" alt=\"Scroll through your OneDrive photo library on one screen, while viewing your selected photo on the other.\" /><span class=\"lia-inline-image-caption\" onclick=\"event.preventDefault();\">Scroll through your OneDrive photo library on one screen, while viewing your selected photo on the other.</span></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"5\"><STRONG>September 2020 teasers</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>Psst, still here? 898_a3b957c889700189.webp","https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/215640i1323F7AE198279D1/image-size/large?v=1.0&px=999":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn77@2020_3/2020/09/05/08-50-02-975_9b704a6c33e0b9a9.webp","https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/215641i1328C43B9EB9FB51/image-size/large?v=1.0&px=999":null},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295794917},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:49:54","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:49:54","title":"SharePoint Online: News from associated sites are not displayed in the hub News Webpart","link":"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/microsoft-sharepoint-blog/sharepoint-online-news-from-associated-sites-are-not-displayed/ba-p/1254333","description":"<H2><FONT size=\"7\">Summary</FONT></H2>\n<P>I recently worked on a case where News from associated sites are not displayed in the hub News Webpart.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"1.png\" style=\"width: 539px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/179568iAB38FB51C7E47446/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"1.png\" alt=\"1.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>This took several months to resolve due to the complexity of hub news webpart and how it integrates with the Search Engine to retrieve and display news from the associated sites.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Before getting into the problem, just providing a quick example of the News webpart configuration with a Hub Site.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Hub Site Example: The following image shows a Hub site named “hubsite” and 2 associated sites (“hubsitechild1” and hubsitechild2”)</P>\n<DIV id=\"tinyMceEditorMike Lee (BOSTON)_1\" class=\"mceNonEditable lia-copypaste-placeholder\">&nbsp;</DIV>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"2.png\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/179557iF53939A3027E199F/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"2.png\" alt=\"2.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Posting News items from the Hub:</P>\n<DIV id=\"tinyMceEditorMike Lee (BOSTON)_2\" class=\"mceNonEditable lia-copypaste-placeholder\">&nbsp;</DIV>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"3.png\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/179558iE9DA0EAAC9A92ACB/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"3.png\" alt=\"3.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>This is what the News Webpart looks like from the root Hub Site:</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"4.png\" style=\"width: 302px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/179559i925FE6DEBCFB8787/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"4.png\" alt=\"4.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Now let’s look at a child site:</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>By default, the News Webpart will only show news from the current site:</P>\n<DIV id=\"tinyMceEditorMike Lee (BOSTON)_4\" class=\"mceNonEditable lia-copypaste-placeholder\">&nbsp;</DIV>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"5.png\" style=\"width: 304px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/179560i6DBDCEBCD5727F5B/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"5.png\" alt=\"5.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Site Admins will need to change this Webpart to view news from the Hub or any associated Hub site. In this example I will choose the “Hubsite”.</P>\n<DIV id=\"tinyMceEditorMike Lee (BOSTON)_5\" class=\"mceNonEditable lia-copypaste-placeholder\">&nbsp;</DIV>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"6.png\" style=\"width: 316px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/179561iECE0C432513E3DF4/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"6.png\" alt=\"6.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>With this configuration “Hubsitechild1” will display News posts from the Hub site</P>\n<DIV id=\"tinyMceEditorMike Lee (BOSTON)_6\" class=\"mceNonEditable lia-copypaste-placeholder\">&nbsp;</DIV>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"7.png\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/179562iD7F2614018FFF830/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"7.png\" alt=\"7.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Note: Since the retrieval of the new posts are based on search, you will not see new posts show up in the news webpart for about 5-15 minutes.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>How does it work?</STRONG></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"13.PNG\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/179723iF9B6C27E64F1A5D2/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"13.PNG\" alt=\"13.PNG\" /></span></P>\n<OL>\n<LI>The News Webpart triggers a request to the SP Home Microservice with “DepartmentID”</LI>\n</OL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P class=\"lia-align-left lia-indent-padding-left-60px\">Example:</P>\n<P class=\"lia-align-left lia-indent-padding-left-60px\"><A href=\"https://sphome_base_url/api/v1/news/hub/filtered?departmentId=47060b5d-eb3a-4f7b-a1c0-421fc86cd0f6&amp;start=0&amp;count=13\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://sphome_base_url/api/v1/news/hub/filtered?departmentId=47060b5d-eb3a-4f7b-a1c0-421fc86cd0f6&amp;start=0&amp;count=13</A></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-60px\">Note: The DepartmentID will be the Site ID of the root hub site.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<OL start=\"2\">\n<LI>The SP Home Micrososervice then calls the Search service with “ContentTypeId”, “PromotedState”, “DepartmentId” to retrieve the News items.</LI>\n</OL>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">&nbsp;</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">Example:</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">&nbsp;</P>\n<PRE class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">GET: https://tenant.sharepoint.com/search/_api/search/query?querytext='(*)'&amp;QueryTemplate='PromotedState:2 AND ContentTypeId:0x0101009D1CB255DA76424F860D91F20E6C4118* AND (DepartmentId:47060b5d-eb3a-4f7b-a1c0-421fc86cd0f6 OR DepartmentId:{47060b5d-eb3a-4f7b-a1c0-421fc86cd0f6})'&amp;Properties='ClientFunction:HubNewsArticles ,EnableDynamicGroups:True'&amp;ClientType='SPHomePagesWeb'&amp;SelectProperties='DocID,Path,DocID,SiteID,NormSiteId,WebID,NormWebId,GroupID,Title,Description,PictureThumbnailURL,AuthorOWSUSER,SiteTitle,SPSiteUrl,SiteLogo,PromotedState,FirstPublishedDate,UniqueId,ViewCountLifetime,SiteTemplate,IsExternalContent,SPWebUrl,ContentTypeId,Language,Color,ListItemID,DepartmentId'&amp;SourceId='8413cd39-2156-4e00-b54d-11efd9abdb89'&amp;Sortlist='FirstPublishedDate:1'&amp;BypassResultTypes=true&amp;TrimDuplicates=true&amp;EnableQueryRules=false&amp;EnableSorting=true&amp;StartRow=0&amp;RowLimit=13</PRE>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<OL start=\"3\">\n<LI>The Search results are sent back to the News Webpart and displayed as configured.</LI>\n</OL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">However, in the case that I was working, the Webpart was not displaying any news, even though the Search request was correct.</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">&nbsp;</P>\n<H2><FONT size=\"7\">Cause</FONT></H2>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>We found that the default Search Schema had been modified either manually or by a 3<SUP>rd</SUP> party product. In this case the managed property “&nbsp;AuthorOWSUSER” is used to locate News items. If the value of this property is unexpected or NULL, Hub News items will not be displayed within the Webpart.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Here is the default setting for the “AuthorOWSUSER “managed property.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"8.png\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/179563iCFB725FE60B9B608/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"8.png\" alt=\"8.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"14.png\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/179724iF41784DFE7EB10E2/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"14.png\" alt=\"14.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>As you can see there are 2 crawled properties by default.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<UL>\n<LI>ows_q_USER__AuthorByline</LI>\n<LI>ows_q_USER_Author</LI>\n</UL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>If either one of these crawled properties are missing, Hub News will not be displayed.</P>\n<P>Also, we found that in some cases there is a new managed property that uses “AuthorOWSUSER” as an alias.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"9.png\" style=\"width: 2489px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/179564iACFE570FE4D7E771/image-dimensions/2489x55?v=1.0\" width=\"2489\" height=\"55\" title=\"9.png\" alt=\"9.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<H2><FONT size=\"7\">Resolution</FONT></H2>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>To resolve this issue, simply fix the modified search schema, which can be modified at the tenant level or the site collection level&nbsp;.</P>\n<P>The AuthorOWSUSER property exists at both tenant level and site level.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>How do we reach tenant level settings?</STRONG></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<OL>\n<LI>Copy this URL and open in the new tab where tenant admin is already signed in <A href=\"https://admin.microsoft.com/sharepoint?page=classicfeatures&amp;modern=true\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://admin.microsoft.com/sharepoint?page=classicfeatures&amp;modern=true</A><SPAN>.</SPAN></LI>\n<LI>Under <STRONG>Search</STRONG>, select <STRONG>Open</STRONG>.</LI>\n<LI>Select <STRONG>Manage Search Schema</STRONG> on the search administration page.</LI>\n</OL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>How do we reach site level settings?</STRONG></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<OL>\n<LI>On one of your affected hub sites, select&nbsp;<EM>Settings,</EM> and then select&nbsp;<EM>Site Settings</EM>. If you don't see&nbsp;<EM>Site settings</EM>, select&nbsp;<EM>Site information</EM>, and then select&nbsp;<EM>View all site settings</EM>.</LI>\n</OL>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\"><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"15.png\" style=\"width: 560px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/179732i5EBDE61E435153C6/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"15.png\" alt=\"15.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<OL start=\"2\">\n<LI>Under&nbsp;<EM>Site Collection Administration</EM>, select<EM>&nbsp;Search Schema</EM>.</LI>\n</OL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<OL start=\"3\">\n<LI>At this point your URL should look like this <A href=\"https://tenant-name.sharepoint.com/sites/Hub-SITE-NAME/_layouts/15/listmanagedproperties.aspx?level=sitecol\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://TENANT-NAME.sharepoint.com/sites/Hub-SITE-NAME/_layouts/15/listmanagedproperties.aspx?level=sitecol</A></LI>\n</OL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>After opening the managed properties list at the tenant/hub site level:</STRONG></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">1. Search for “AuthorOWSUSER”</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\"><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"16.png\" style=\"width: 469px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/179738i96B94B45625361DC/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"16.png\" alt=\"16.png\" /></span></P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">2. You see all matches, including any custom managed properties that set <STRONG>AuthorOWSUSER</STRONG> as an alias.</P>\n<DIV id=\"tinyMceEditorMike Lee (BOSTON)_2\" class=\"mceNonEditable lia-copypaste-placeholder\">&nbsp;</DIV>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\"><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"17.png\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/179729i2B2B2EDC11804CB4/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"17.png\" alt=\"17.png\" /></span></P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">&nbsp;</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">3. Locate the problematic Managed property and correct the issue by deleting the property or changing the alias. In this example, I will change the alias of “<STRONG>Thiswillbreaknews</STRONG>”.</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\"><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"18.png\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/179735i73FC9756953CF468/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"18.png\" alt=\"18.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">4. Make sure <STRONG>AuthorOWSUSER</STRONG> is mapped to “<STRONG>ows_q_USER__AuthorByline</STRONG>” and “ows_q_USER_Author”, if the mapping is incorrect, fix it.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Please Note: Since these some of these properties are used in real-time, the problem should be resolved almost immediately.&nbsp; In a worst-case scenario, you will have to re-index the site&nbsp;, wait for Search to complete (about 15 minutes), then re-create the News Webpart.</P>\n<P><STRONG>&nbsp;</STRONG></P>\n<P><STRONG>Steps to Re-index the site:</STRONG></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<OL>\n<LI>On the hub site site, select <STRONG>Settings</STRONG>\n<DIV id=\"tinyMceEditorMike Lee (BOSTON)_4\" class=\"mceNonEditable lia-copypaste-placeholder\">&nbsp;</DIV>\n<P>and then select <STRONG>Site settings</STRONG>. If you don't see <STRONG>Site settings</STRONG>, select <STRONG>Site information</STRONG>, and then select <STRONG>View all site settings</STRONG>.</P>\n</LI>\n<LI>Under <STRONG>Search</STRONG>, click <STRONG>Search and offline availability</STRONG>.</LI>\n<LI>In the <STRONG>Reindex site</STRONG> section, click <STRONG>Reindex site</STRONG>.</LI>\n</OL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<H1>More everything&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN class=\"brand\">Microsoft 365</SPAN><SPAN>. &nbsp;&nbsp;</SPAN></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><SPAN>Waldek and the PnP CLI team are gearing up to ship v3.0 of PnP CLI
