Please use&nbsp;<A href=\"https://twitter.com/search?q=%23pnpweekly\" target=\"_self\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer noopener noreferrer noopener noreferrer\">#PnPWeekly hashtag</A>&nbsp;in the Twitter for letting us know the content which you have created.&nbsp;</SPAN></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P class=\"\">As always, if you need help on an issue, want to share a discovery, or just want to say: “<EM>Job well done</EM>”, please reach out to Vesa, to Waldek or to your PnP Community.</P>\n<P class=\"\">&nbsp;</P>\n<P class=\"\"><EM>Sharing is caring!</EM></P>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Wed, 02 Sep 2020 18:52:43 +0000","feedId":13333,"bgimg":"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/216107iA58689B8D4A767BA/image-size/large?v=1.0&px=999","linkMd5":"67f976f2f8c6a4a6d4f5dfd5859ea03c","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn19@2020_5/2020/09/05/08-49-55-643_55745c402eab4f1f.webp","destWidth":998,"destHeight":562,"sourceBytes":57654,"destBytes":39582,"author":"Vesa Juvonen","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/216107iA58689B8D4A767BA/image-size/large?v=1.0&px=999":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn19@2020_5/2020/09/05/08-49-55-643_55745c402eab4f1f.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295794892},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:49:54","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:49:54","title":"Troubleshooting Explorer view and mapped drives to SharePoint","link":"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/microsoft-sharepoint-blog/troubleshooting-explorer-view-and-mapped-drives-to-sharepoint/ba-p/1185909","description":"<P><FONT size=\"5\"><STRONG>Overview</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>Distributed Authoring and Versioning (DAV) is an extension of the HTTP protocol that allows the user to interact with and manipulate files stored on a web server. The Windows implementation of the DAV protocol as a mini-redirector is handled by the WebClient service. As a mini-redirector it allows native Windows applications to interact with the remote file system through native networking API calls similar to the local file system and other remote file storage servers (such as CIFS and SMB). This is typically seen by the user as mapped drives or a Windows Explorer view.</P>\n<P>Note: Although Windows 7 and Windows Server 2008 R2 exited support Jan 14, 2020, there are still many machines that will not be upgraded so the information below will still reference issues and resolutions that may be relevant to those operating systems.</P>\n<P>Following the re-writing of the service in Windows Vista, the feature set was considered mature and further changes were primarily bug fixes and security updates. The service consists of webclnt.dll, davclnt.dll and mrxdav.sys (minimum version in Windows 7 should be 6.1.7601.23542) but is also reliant upon webio.dll, winhttp.dll (<FONT size=\"4\">minimum</FONT> version in Windows 7 should be 6.1.7601.23375)&nbsp;and shell32.dll (minimum version in Windows 7 should be 6.1.7601.22498).</P>\n<P>With those files at their latest versions, undesired behavior is typically due to a misconfiguration or a limitation of the implementation.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"5\"><STRONG>Common issues with Explorer view</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P><FONT size=\"4\"><STRONG>A Root site must exist</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>There are certain circumstances where the WebClient will walk the path as it would for an SMB file share. Although the path segment does not have to allow WebDAV, it must be present. See <A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/kb/2625462\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/kb/2625462</A> - SharePoint: Office client integration errors when no root site exists</P>\n<P><STRONG>Action:</STRONG> If a Root site is missing, create one. The users do not necessarily need access and there does not even need to be a Site Template selected; it just needs to exist.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"4\"><STRONG>Requests issuing OPTIONS and PROPFIND requests must be responded to with a success or an authentication response.</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>If the OPTIONS call receives a 200 Success response, the Webclient (and Office client) will assume that WebDAV is supported (even if the returned list of Allowed verbs does not include WebDAV verbs).</P>\n<P>The PROPFIND request expects a 207 Multi-Status response as a success.</P>\n<P>A 401 or 403 response is an indication of inadequate authentication information. A valid 401 response will include WWW-Authenticate headers that identify the type of authentication that is accepted (i.e. Negotiate, NTLM, Basic, Digest, Bearer). If a 403 response is received normally that means the resource is present but there are inadequate privileges to interact with it. Unlike the 401 response, submission of additional authentication will not provide access. A few years ago the 403 status code began being used for responses where Forms Based Authentication (FBA) and claims authentication is used but the requesting agent is unable to process a 302 redirect to a login page (see the MS-OFBA Protocol specification).</P>\n<P>If these are not the responses received by the client then typically the request is being blocked, either by the HTTP verbs setting of the Request Filtering in IIS, a URL-Rewrite rule or perhaps by a device in the middle. The most common alternate responses are 404 Not Found if the verb is blocked or a 302 Redirect to a login page for third party authentication providers that do not adhere to the MS-OFBA specification.</P>\n<P><STRONG>Action</STRONG>: Verify that the request is making it to the server with simultaneous network traces or check the IIS logs. If the IIS logs show the response is coming from the server, open IIS Manager and check the HTTP verbs tab in Request Filtering. If the verbs are not listed there, then you may need to collect Failed Request Tracing to identify the source of the response. The full list of WebDAV verbs that need to be allowed are referenced elsewhere on this page.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"4\"><STRONG>Client integration must be enabled at the web application level and the 'UseRemoteAPIs' permission must be 'true'</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>If Client integration is not enabled, the OPTIONS request is not sent, and the client will assume WebDAV is not supported.</P>\n<P><STRONG>Action:</STRONG> Enable Client Integration (located at CA &gt; Web Application Management &gt; Authentication Providers &gt; Zone ) and verify there is no policy disabling the 'UseRemoteAPIs' permission, See <A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/2758444\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/2758444</A> - SharePoint 2013 Disable WebDAV use on SharePoint</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"4\"><STRONG>WebDAV must not be enabled in IIS features of the server</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>If the WebDAV feature is enabled in IIS it will interfere with the SharePoint implementation of the WebDAV handler. See <A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/2171959\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/2171959</A> - Explorer view does not work in some scenarios when the SharePoint farm is on Windows Server 2008 R2 or <A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/2018958\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/2018958</A> - SharePoint 2007 or 2010: Office Documents open ReadOnly from SharePoint site</P>\n<P><STRONG>Action:</STRONG> Remove the WebDAV feature from IIS (this will require a reboot of the server).</P>\n<UL>\n<LI>Windows Server 2008 R2 - In Server Manager go to Roles-&gt;Web Server IIS section, Click Remove Role Services and Uncheck 'Web Server\\Common HTTP Features\\WebDAV Publishing'</LI>\n<LI>Windows Server 2012 - Uncheck 'WebDAV Publishing' in Server Manager-&gt;Manage-&gt;Remove Roles and Features then Web Server IIS section-&gt;Web Server-&gt;Common HTTP Features</LI>\n<LI>Windows Server 2012 R2 - Uncheck 'WebDAV Publishing' in Server Manager-&gt;Manage-&gt;Remove Roles and Features then Web Server IIS section-&gt;Web Server-&gt;Common HTTP Features</LI>\n</UL>\n<P><FONT size=\"4\"><STRONG>If FBA/Claims authentication is being used, the site must be in an IE security zone where Enable Protect Mode is not checked (by default that is the Trusted zone) and persistent cookies must be used.</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>When Forms Based Authentication (FBA) or Claims Authentication is used, the client presents its authentication through a cookie. Since the WebClient service cannot show a login page, it must rely on the authentication cookie from the browser. Sharing cookies retained solely in memory (session cookies) between processes would be a security violation so, in order for the WebClient service to acquire the cookie, it must be created as a persistent cookie and stored in a location shared where other processes can access it.</P>\n<P>A persistent cookie is one created with an expires time. This is observable in the response when the Set-Cookie header is sent from the authenticating server to the client. Frequently the cookie name is FedAuth, but it does not have to be. Normally an authentication cookie will be complex enough that it will look like a VERY long string of random characters. If the expires attribute is not on the Set-Cookie header it is a session cookie and not a persistent cookie. Making the cookie persistent is considered a security reduction but one that is necessary in order for the WebClient service to acquire it (there was a period where a callback function in MSO.dll shared session cookies with the service but it was not intended for that purpose, is unreliable and should not be happening in current products).</P>\n<P>The WebClient service calls the InternetGetCookieEx function to read the cookies from the cookie jar (which is one reason why Explorer view only works with Internet Explorer). Applications can only share cookies if the site is not in a zone where Protect Mode is enabled. By default, that is the Trusted zone, but the configuration can be changed so always verify the Enable Protect Mode checkbox.</P>\n<P>For more, see \"WebClient service does not support Session Cookies\" - <A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/kb/2985898\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/kb/2985898</A> . This is also documented in the Whitepaper Implementing \"Persistent Cookies in SharePoint 2010 Products\" <A href=\"https://download.microsoft.com/download/9/F/6/9F69FEBA-614B-483F-9CF2-60225D75E81E/persistent-cookies-whitepaper.docx\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://download.microsoft.com/download/9/F/6/9F69FEBA-614B-483F-9CF2-60225D75E81E/persistent-cookies-whitepaper.docx</A></P>\n<P><STRONG>Action:</STRONG></P>\n<UL>\n<LI>Verify the cookie is persistent (you may need a Fiddler, netsh or another network capture to verify the Set-Cookie header).</LI>\n</UL>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">The login form may have a \"Keep me signed in\" or \"Sign me in automatically' checkbox that the user must enable. If the user has no option, and if SharePoint is creating the cookie, then you may need to use the PowerShell to enable it from the SharePoint Management Shell:</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-60px\">$sts = Get-SPSecurityTokenServiceConfig</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-60px\">$sts.UseSessionCookies = $false</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-60px\">$sts.Update()</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-60px\">iisreset</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">&nbsp;</P>\n<UL>\n<LI>Verify the site is in a zone where 'Enable Protect Mode' is unchecked - see <A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/932118\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/932118</A> - Persistent cookies are not shared between Internet Explorer and Office applications</LI>\n</UL>\n<P><FONT size=\"4\"><STRONG>WebClient binaries need to be current, especially for Windows 7.</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>There have been several updates to the WebClient binaries over the years. See the Overview on this page for the list of binaries and recommended minimum versions. Some critical changes have been regarding cookie handling and TLS support. In some versions of Windows 7, persistent cookies were not passed until a 401 or 403 response was received. This broke the login process for third-party authentication providers who did not differentiate between browser and non-browser user agents. Also, the Windows 7 WebClient used default security protocols that maxed out at TLS 1.0 (see issue #9 below). Another issue that was fixed was the use of Server Name Indicator (SNI) - see #8 below.</P>\n<P><STRONG>Action:</STRONG> verify that the WebClient DLLs (and those supporting them) are current. See the Overview above for more but this is becoming less of an issue as the latest security updates generally have the necessary files.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"4\"><STRONG>If the site is using Windows authentication and the host name is FQDN, then credentials are not passed</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>The WebClient service does not leverage the Internet Settings Zone Manager to identify when it is safe to automatically send credentials so by default credentials were automatically sent to only sites without periods in the host name. Since companies frequently use fully qualified domain names (FQDN) internally as well, another method was created to allow administrators to identify when it was safe to automatically send credentials. This is done by using the AuthForwardServerList registry key under the WebClient service hive. See <A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/kb/943280\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://support.microsoft.com/kb/943280</A> -Prompt for credentials when you access WebDav-based FQDN sites in Windows.</P>\n<P class=\"lia-align-center\"><STRONG>Note: This KB applies to all versions of Windows after Windows Vista SP1</STRONG></P>\n<P><STRONG>Action:</STRONG> Add the site to the AuthForwardServerList. This is a client-side registry key. Also be sure that the Multi-SZ reg entry has a return at the end - some versions of Windows will allow adding the entry without a return but without the return the key is not read properly</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"4\"><STRONG>If Server Name Indication (SNI) is enabled anywhere in the IIS bindings, then the client cannot connect (Windows 7 only).</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>If multiple certificates are used for different web applications on the IIS\\SharePoint server then either the server must bind the web application to different IP addresses or implement SNI. Some good reading on SharePoint and SNI can be found at <A href=\"https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/sambetts/2015/02/13/running-multiple-sharepoint-ssl-websites-on-separate-ssl-certificates-using-server-name-indication\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/sambetts/2015/02/13/running-multiple-sharepoint-ssl-websites-on-separate-ssl-certificates-using-server-name-indication</A></P>\n<P><EM>Windows 7 did not initially implement support for SNI but this was corrected when the service changed the way WinHTTP was called in MS15-089: Vulnerability in WebDAV could allow security feature bypass: August 11, 2015</EM></P>\n<P><STRONG>Action:</STRONG> Update the client to a supported version or disable SNI in IIS.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"4\"><STRONG>Explorer view fails if the TLS handshake cannot complete (most commonly Windows 7).</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>If only TLS 1.1 and/or 1.2 are enabled (and earlier versions disallowed), then Windows 7 clients will need the latest WebClient and WinHttp binary updates as well as the registry edits for WinHTTP that change the default security protocols to allow TLS 1.1/1.2 - <A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/kb/3140245\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/kb/3140245</A></P>\n<P>Initially the Windows 7 WebClient service set the list of available security providers when opening the connection through WinHTTP but it had a maximum value of TLS 1.0. Later, the service stopped setting a specific list and just took the WinHTTP system default security settings (<A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/kb/3076949\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://support.microsoft.com/kb/3076949</A> - MS15-089: Vulnerability in WebDAV could allow security feature bypass: August 11, 2015). Unfortunately, this did not help since the default was SSL 3 and TLS 1.0 (the system default beginning with Windows 8.1 includes TLS 1.0, 1.1 and 1.2). This limitation was removed when an update came out that allowed the 'system default' settings be changed - <A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/3140245\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/3140245</A> - Update to enable TLS 1.1 and TLS 1.2 as a default secure protocols in WinHTTP in Windows.</P>\n<P><STRONG>Action:</STRONG> Ensure the client and server systems have the necessary registry settings and binaries to allow a common TLS version (the higher the better). In addition to checking the SCHANNEL\\Protocol client and server settings, check for the WinHttp registry settings in Internet Settings as these will be used as override values in updated Windows 7 machines and all supported operating systems. Updated client binaries include WinHTTP/WebIO in addition to the WebClient files. See the Overview above for the list of files and minimum versions for Windows 7.</P>\n<P><STRONG>Note:</STRONG> The update 3140245 has registry entries that also need to be set.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"4\"><STRONG>There can be no certificate errors. The site name must match the certificate, not be expired and be trusted.</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>This affects all versions of Windows clients. The WebClient service has no tolerance for certificate errors. Use the browser to see if the certificate is reporting errors. Alternatively view the certificate to verify the certificate is in the valid date range, has a trusted certification path and has a Subject or Subject Alternative Name that matches the site.</P>\n<P><STRONG>Action:</STRONG> Replace the certificate with a valid certificate.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"4\"><STRONG>If the server has custom IIS headers, the custom header name cannot contain spaces.</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>Custom headers are an excellent tool for troubleshooting through load balancers. And a custom header with a unique value on each WFE and then the traces can tell you which server responded in the farm. However, be careful that the custom header name does NOT contain any spaces. The UI will allow them and there is no documentation that states they are prohibited but spaces will cause a client-side failure while processing the response. This was discovered when OPTIONS and PROPFIND calls were failing; the client terminated the session after receiving the first packet of the response even while additional packets were being sent.</P>\n<P><STRONG>Action:</STRONG> Remove or rename the custom IIS header. A suggestion would be to either remove the space or replace it with an underscore; the underscore is typically a more aesthetic change.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"4\"><STRONG>PROPFIND and PROPPATCH responses must contain valid XML and not be Content-encoded (g-zip)</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>If the WebClient service receives a response to a PROPFIND or PROPPATCH that does not contain a valid XML structure it can result in unusual behavior possibly even generating undesired credential prompts (see <A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/2019105\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/2019105</A> - Authentication requests when you open Office documents).</P>\n<P>The WebClient service cannot handle a response that has GZIP encoded the body. This was discovered in a case where an Akamai router/load balancer was GZIP encoding the response (it worked when Fiddler was used because Fiddler was decompressing the file). This will almost certainly be a device in the middle (it is unconfirmed if enabling IIS compression on a SharePoint server will cause this.</P>\n<P><STRONG>Action:</STRONG> Identify the device doing compression and disable compression for PROPFIND/PROPPATCH requests.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"4\"><STRONG>Unable to create new files or folders</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>When the WebClient service creates a new file or folder it will first check for the presence of an existing order to prompt for an override if necessary. If a custom 404 handler has been put it place it may intercept the necessary 404 response and the WebClient service will fail to create the new file or folder..</P>\n<P><STRONG>Action:</STRONG> The custom 404 handler must either be removed or updated ignore the WebClient requests. Modifying the custom handler to not engage when the User Agent string is <STRONG>Microsoft-WebDAV-MiniRedir</STRONG> is one way the requests can be filtered.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"4\"><STRONG>Verbs needs for WebDAV to work</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>For WebDAV communication to work properly, the WebDAV verbs (also called Methods) must be allowed by the server. The RFC 4918 internet specification includes: PROPFIND, PROPPATCH, MKCOL, COPY, MOVE, LOCK, UNLOCK. In addition to those, the HTTP methods of OPTIONS, HEAD, PUT and DELETE are frequently associated with the WebDAV protocol and should be allowed as well.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"4\"><STRONG>UNC paths</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>When the WebClient service translates between the HTTP protocol to UNC the conversion is fairly straightforward. A path like <A href=\"http://server/site\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">http://server/site</A>&nbsp;would become \\\\server\\site . HTTPS adds an additional suffix - <A href=\"https://server/site\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://server/site</A>&nbsp;becomes \\\\server<STRONG>@ssl</STRONG>\\site.</P>\n<P>If the WebDAV share is at the root, the UNC will need a virtual share (UNC requires a \\\\server\\share minimum). The 'virtual share' is DavWWWRoot. Example: <A href=\"http://server\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">http://server</A>&nbsp;would be \\\\server\\DavWWWRoot .</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"5\"><STRONG>Configuration changes needed to support large file uploads</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>When configuring an environment to support large file uploads to SharePoint through Windows Explorer, there are four settings to adjust:</P>\n<P>On the server:</P>\n<UL>\n<LI>Increase the SharePoint Maximum upload size on the web app (max of 2047 mb)</LI>\n<LI>Increase the IIS Connection Time-out to a value longer than the time needed to upload (default of 120 seconds - max of 65535 or 0xffff ).</LI>\n</UL>\n<P>On the client:</P>\n<P>There are two settings under the WebClient service registry (HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SYSTEM\\CurrentControlSet\\Services\\WebClient\\Parameters):</P>\n<UL>\n<LI>Increase the <STRONG>FileSizeLimitInBytes</STRONG> (default of 50 mb - max of 0xffffffff or 4 gb)&nbsp;<A title=\"KB 2668751\" href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/2668751\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/2668751</A>&nbsp;</LI>\n<LI>Increased the <STRONG>SendReceiveTimeoutInSec</STRONG> to a value longer than the time needed to upload (default of 60 seconds - max of 4294967295 0xfffffff).</LI>\n</UL>\n<P><FONT size=\"5\"><STRONG>Calculating the time needed to upload a file via Explorer view</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>Performance of file uploads via a mapped drive to SharePoint or Explorer view is limited by the WebClient service. The approximate maximum throughput is 8 kb per RTT.</P>\n<P>Throughput is amount of data divided by time.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>If the server allows a ping, you can get an average RTT with the following PowerShell:</P>\n<P>$rtt = (Test-Connection -ComputerName myservername | Measure-Object -Property ResponseTime -Average).Average</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Note: if the server does not allow a normal ping or if you want a more exact RTT measurement, you can use the PSPing utility from SysInternals - <A href=\"https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/sysinternals/psping\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/sysinternals/psping</A></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>The amount of time it would take to upload a 2047 Mb file with an average RTT of 1.75 ms would be:</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">Filesize / 8kb * RTT</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">2,146,435,072&nbsp;bytes / 8,192 bytes * .00175 seconds</P>\n<P class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\">or approximately 459 seconds</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"5\"><STRONG>Library contents do not display in Explorer view</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>This issue can occur for a couple of known reasons.</P>\n<P>First, if there are too many files in the library folder, the Explorer view display as an empty folder. This problem can occur if the size of all the file attributes (the PROPFIND response) returned by the WebDAV server is larger than expected. By default, this size is limited to 1 MB.</P>\n<P>The client registry value <STRONG>FileAttributesLimitInBytes</STRONG> can be increased to accommodate the amount of properties returned (the suggested estimate is approximately 1k per file so for 20,000 files, use a value of 20000000). For more details, see <A href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/912152\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/912152</A> - \"You cannot access a WebDAV Web folder from a Windows-based client computer\".</P>\n<P>The preferred resolution would be to reduce the number of files in a folder; SharePoint performs best with less than 5000 item in a view but Explorer view will request all files and possibly exceed the normal view settings.</P>\n<P>Second, if the combined length of path and filename of any file in the folder exceeds the maximum supported by the Windows Explorer (approx. 255), then no items will be displayed until the folder and/or filename is shortened. You may have to use the SharePoint web interface to make the change.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><FONT size=\"5\"><STRONG>Consider using a diagnostic to examine the client</STRONG></FONT></P>\n<P>Here is a diagnostic script that can help identify the current configuration and some common problems (do a 'Save Target as' on the [Raw] button) : <A href=\"https://github.com/edbarnes-msft/DrDAV/blob/master/Test_MsDavConnection.ps1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://github.com/edbarnes-msft/DrDAV/blob/master/Test_MsDavConnection.ps1</A></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Thu, 27 Aug 2020 22:47:59 +0000","feedId":13333,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"2013a3b861cb9db4fec954532035e8e3","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"Ed_Barnes","publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295794894},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:49:54","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:49:54","title":"M365 Administrator Feedback Request | SharePoint Support Central Experience","link":"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/microsoft-sharepoint-blog/m365-administrator-feedback-request-sharepoint-support-central/ba-p/1534211","description":"<P>\n Every month, thousands of M365 Administrators turn to \n <STRONG>\n  Support Central\n </STRONG> to engage in various self-help options. Support issues can vary in complexity and while sometimes you want to talk to a support agent directly, in other situations it's more convenient to solve the topic independently via articles , diagnostics or other self-help solutions. In one of my previous posts, I explained how administrators can engage with Support Central to run \n <A href=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/sharepoint-support-blog/how-to-troubleshoot-issues-in-sharepoint-online-and-onedrive/ba-p/637974\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">\n  diagnostics for SharePoint and OneDrive\n </A>. To access this area, simply navigate to \n <A href=\"https://admin.microsoft.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">\n  <STRONG>\n   Microsoft 365 Admin Center\n  </STRONG>\n </A> &gt; \n <STRONG>\n  Support\n </STRONG> &gt; \n <STRONG>\n  New Service Request\n </STRONG>. Once you are in Support Central you will receive self-help solutions based on your specific query as well as have the option to engage directly with agents. These solutions, based on the query you provided, are run through telemetry and machine learning to provide you with the best possible answer. Based on this information, we not only point you to further relevant resources - such as diagnostics, videos, or help articles - but in many cases, we also directly recommend a specific action for you in-line to solve the problem.\n</P> \n<P>\n <EM>\n  &nbsp;\n  <span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-center\" image-alt=\"SupportCentral .gif\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/206530i6F8ACC872051387B/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"SupportCentral .gif\" alt=\"SupportCentral .gif\" /></span>\n </EM>\n</P> \n<P>\n <EM>\n  Quickly engage with support central via the “New Service Request” button in the M365 Admin Center.\n </EM>\n</P> \n<P>\n &nbsp;\n</P> \n<P>\n <span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"SupportCentralSharePoint.PNG\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/206537iFDF9FFFCB331644C/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"SupportCentralSharePoint.PNG\" alt=\"SupportCentralSharePoint.PNG\" /></span>\n</P> \n<P>\n <EM>\n  Get solutions specifically catered to your help query based on machine learning. 16:49:54","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:49:54","title":"Awareness of temporary adjustments in SharePoint Online","link":"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/microsoft-sharepoint-blog/awareness-of-temporary-adjustments-in-sharepoint-online/ba-p/1250603","description":"<P>On March 24<SUP>th</SUP> we shared in an announcement in the M365 message center (<A href=\"https://admin.microsoft.com/Adminportal/Home?source=applauncher#/MessageCenter?id=MC207439\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">MC207439</A>) details around temporary adjustments we are making to select capabilities in SharePoint Online and OneDrive.</P>\n<P><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}\" data-wac-het=\"1\">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>\n<P><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">During these unprecedented times, we are taking steps to ensure that SharePoint Online and OneDrive services remain available and reliable for your users who depend on the service more than ever in remote work scenarios.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}\" data-wac-het=\"1\">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>\n<P><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}\" data-wac-het=\"1\">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>\n<PRE><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}\" data-wac-het=\"1\"><STRONG>Note:&nbsp;</STRONG>These&nbsp;temporary feature&nbsp;adjustments&nbsp;may&nbsp;be in place during business hours in your&nbsp;tenant's&nbsp;region.&nbsp;&nbsp;</SPAN></PRE>\n<P><STRONG><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">C</SPAN></STRONG><STRONG><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">ontent migration, Data Loss Prevention (DLP), and backup solutions</SPAN></STRONG><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}\" data-wac-het=\"1\">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>\n<P><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">Many SharePoint Online and OneDrive customers run business-critical applications against the service that run in the background. These include content migration, Data Loss Prevention (DLP), apps that scan the service and backup solutions.&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}\" data-wac-het=\"1\">&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">In support of the objective to remain highly available</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">,&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">we are&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">moving some operations to regional evening and weekend hours.</SPAN></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">Users may observe:</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}\" data-wac-het=\"1\">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>\n<UL>\n<LI data-leveltext=\"\" data-font=\"Symbol\" data-listid=\"1\" aria-setsize=\"-1\" data-aria-posinset=\"1\" data-aria-level=\"1\"><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">Migration, DLP and backup solutions may achieve limited throughput during regional weekday daytime hours. During evening and weekend hours for the region, the service will be ready to process a significantly higher&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">volume</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">of requests from background apps.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\" data-wac-het=\"1\">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>\n</UL>\n<P><SPAN data-contrast=\"auto\">Please review the relevant best practice guidance, which describes how to get maximize throughput.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:240,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}\" data-wac-het=\"1\">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>\n<UL>\n<LI data-leveltext=\"\" data-font=\"Symbol\" data-listid=\"10\" aria-setsize=\"-1\" data-aria-posinset=\"2\" data-aria-level=\"1\"><A href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/sharepointmigration/sharepoint-online-and-onedrive-migration-speed\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">Migration performance guidance</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast=\"auto\"> , which includes an </SPAN><A href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/sharepointmigration/sharepoint-online-and-onedrive-migration-speed\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">FAQ &amp; Troubleshooting section</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast=\"auto\"> </SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559685&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:120,&quot;335559739&quot;:120,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}\" data-wac-het=\"1\">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>\n<LI data-leveltext=\"\" data-font=\"Symbol\" data-listid=\"10\" aria-setsize=\"-1\" data-aria-posinset=\"3\" data-aria-level=\"1\"><SPAN data-contrast=\"auto\">For DLP, Apps that scan the service &amp; Backup apps: </SPAN><A href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/onedrive/developer/rest-api/concepts/scan-guidance?view=odsp-graph-online\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">Best practices for discovering files and detecting changes at scale</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast=\"auto\"> </SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559685&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:60,&quot;335559739&quot;:120,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}\" data-wac-het=\"1\">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>\n</UL>\n<P><STRONG><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">File Management</SPAN></STRONG><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}\" data-wac-het=\"1\">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>\n<P><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">Various&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">background processes to manage new media (images, videos)&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">may&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">now</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">&nbsp;be processed during evening and weekend hours.&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}\" data-wac-het=\"1\">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">Modified processes include:</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}\" data-wac-het=\"1\">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>\n<UL>\n<LI data-leveltext=\"\" data-font=\"Symbol\" data-listid=\"9\" aria-setsize=\"-1\" data-aria-posinset=\"1\" data-aria-level=\"1\"><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">Users may experience reduced video resolution for playback videos.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}\" data-wac-het=\"1\">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>\n<LI data-leveltext=\"\" data-font=\"Symbol\" data-listid=\"9\" aria-setsize=\"-1\" data-aria-posinset=\"1\" data-aria-level=\"1\">\n<P>Customers who use OneDrive Files On-Demand and choose to “display items by using large thumbnails” in Windows Explorer or Mac Finder will see generic icons instead of thumbnails.</P>\n<PRE><STRONG>Note:&nbsp;</STRONG>Photo file thumbnails (jpeg, jpg, png, etc) are <STRONG>not</STRONG> affected by this change.</PRE>\n<P>The affected thumbnail types are categorized as the following:</P>\n<UL>\n<LI>Video and PDF files: pdf, avi, mp4, mov, mpg, etc.</LI>\n<LI>Document files with generators: docx, txt, html, etc.</LI>\n<LI>New extensions likely to be permanently blocked because no thumbnail generator is ever likely to exist:&nbsp; reg|bak|iso|nupkg, etc.</LI>\n<LI>Files types already blocked today because no generator exists: lnk|xlsx|xls|url|exe|zip|rar|rdp|apprefms|msi|website</LI>\n</UL>\n<P>There is no workaround, we&nbsp;will&nbsp;continue listening to feedback and&nbsp;iterate&nbsp;on this approach.&nbsp;&nbsp;</P>\n</LI>\n</UL>\n<P><STRONG><SPAN data-contrast=\"none\">Additional Information&nbsp;</SPAN></STRONG><SPAN data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335551550&quot;:1,&quot;335551620&quot;:1,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:240}\" data-wac-het=\"1\">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>\n<UL>\n<LI><A schedule for SharePoint Online services</SPAN></A></LI>\n<LI data-leveltext=\"\" data-font=\"Symbol\" data-listid=\"11\" aria-setsize=\"-1\" data-aria-posinset=\"1\" data-aria-level=\"1\"><A height=\"56px\">&nbsp;</TD>\n</TR>\n</TBODY>\n</TABLE>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>If you are not sure about a particular endpoint, you can use this powershell to test the endpoint to see which versions of TLS it supports-</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<LI-CODE lang=\"powershell\">&lt;#\nCreated by: whall\nDate Created: 3/25/2020\n\nProduct Area Tags: Connectivity\n\nTechnology Tags: SSL TLS\n\nUse Case: \nShows which version(s) of TLS is supported for a URL\n\nDescription: \nWhen you run this, it checks each TLS type connection to see if it is supported.\n\n\nParameters:\n-url this is the URL of the site you are testing against\n\nKeywords: sockets secure https\n\nCode Example Disclaimer:\nSample Code is provided for the purpose of illustration only and is not intended to be used in a production environment. THIS SAMPLE CODE AND ANY RELATED INFORMATION ARE PROVIDED 'AS IS'\n-This is intended as a sample of how code might be written for a similar purpose and you will need to make changes to fit to your requirements. \n-This code has not been tested.&nbsp; This code is also not to be considered best practices or prescriptive guidance.&nbsp; \n-No debugging or error handling has been implemented.\n-It is highly recommended that you FULLY understand what this code is doing&nbsp; and use this code at your own risk.\n\n#&gt;\n\n#TLS check\nparam([Parameter(Mandatory=$true)][string]$url)\n\nfunction TLSAvailable([string]$url){\n\n\n    Write-Host =======================\n    Write-Host $url\n    Write-Host =======================\n    \n    [System.Net.ServicePointManager]::SecurityProtocol = \"Tls\"\n\n    try{\n    $resp1 = Invoke-WebRequest -uri $url -Method GET -DisableKeepAlive\n    if($resp1.StatusCode -eq 200){\n        Write-Host \"TLS/SSL 1.0 supported\" -ForegroundColor green\n    }\n    }catch {\n        Write-Host \"TLS/SSL 1.0 not supported\" -ForegroundColor Red\n        #$_.Exception\n    }\n\n    [System.Net.ServicePointManager]::SecurityProtocol = \"Tls11\"\n    try{\n    $resp2 = Invoke-WebRequest -uri $url -Method GET -DisableKeepAlive\n    if($resp2.StatusCode -eq 200){\n        Write-Host \"TLS/SSL 1.1 supported\" -ForegroundColor green\n    }\n    }catch {\n            Write-Host \"TLS/SSL 1.1 not supported\" -ForegroundColor Red\n            #$_.Exception\n    }\n\n    [System.Net.ServicePointManager]::SecurityProtocol = \"Tls12\"\n\n    try{\n    $resp3 = Invoke-WebRequest -uri $url -Method GET -DisableKeepAlive\n    if($resp3.StatusCode -eq 200){\n        Write-Host \"TLS/SSL 1.2 supported\" -ForegroundColor green\n    }\n    }catch{\n            Write-Host \"TLS/SSL 1.2 not supported\" -ForegroundColor Red\n            #$_.Exception\n    }\n    Write-Host =======================\n\n}\n\nTLSAvailable -url $url\n</LI-CODE>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<H3>Azure Web Application Services</H3>\n<P>If you are running a .NET web application in the Azure web application services, you can set the TLS level under the application settings as below-</P>\n<DIV id=\"tinyMceEditorSPDev_Support_0\" class=\"mceNonEditable lia-copypaste-placeholder\">&nbsp;</DIV>\n<DIV id=\"tinyMceEditorSPDev_Support_1\" class=\"mceNonEditable lia-copypaste-placeholder\">&nbsp;</DIV>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"Annotation 2020-08-28 133047.png\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/215298iA6FF64F5CB4797BF/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"Annotation 2020-08-28 133047.png\" alt=\"Annotation 2020-08-28 133047.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;&nbsp;</P>\n<H3>.NET Framework Code</H3>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">If you are compiling your code for .NET framework 4.7 (4.7.1 for WCF apps) or later, it will use the default TLS version for the OS.</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">&nbsp;</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">If you complied to a previous .NET framework version, it will use older versions of TLS unless you apply the right patch, and use one of the following methods-</P>\n<OL style=\"margin-left: .375in; direction: ltr; unicode-bidi: embed; margin-top: 0in; margin-bottom: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;\" type=\"1\">\n<LI style=\"margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; vertical-align: middle;\" value=\"1\"><SPAN style=\"font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;\">Set a registry setting to force all .NET code to use strong cryptography</SPAN></LI>\n<LI style=\"margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; vertical-align: middle;\"><SPAN style=\"font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">Set a config setting for the app context overrides to use the strong cryptography</SPAN></LI>\n<LI style=\"margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; vertical-align: middle;\"><SPAN style=\"font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">Add a line of code to change the TLS version used for HTTPS calls</SPAN></LI>\n</OL>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">&nbsp;</P>\n<H4 style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">Method 1 (System wide registry change)-</H4>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">This enables something called strong cryptography which makes .NET use the strongest cryptography available currently. This affects all .NET applications with one registry change (per CLR version).</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">Enable strong cryptography for .NET CLR 4 versions (64 bit)-</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">Windows Registry Editor Version 5.00</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">[HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SOFTWARE\\Microsoft\\.NETFramework\\v4.0.30319]</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">\"SchUseStrongCrypto\"=dword:00000001</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">[HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SOFTWARE\\Wow6432Node\\Microsoft\\.NETFramework\\v4.0.30319]</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">\"SchUseStrongCrypto\"=dword:00000001</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">&nbsp;</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">Enable strong cryptography for .NET CLR 2 versions (64 bit)-</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">Windows Registry Editor Version 5.00</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">[HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SOFTWARE\\Microsoft\\.NETFramework\\v2.0.50727]</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">\"SchUseStrongCrypto\"=dword:00000001</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">[HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SOFTWARE\\Wow6432Node\\Microsoft\\.NETFramework\\v2.0.50727]</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">\"SchUseStrongCrypto\"=dword:00000001</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">&nbsp;</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">&nbsp;</P>\n<H4 style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">Method 2 (Config file change)-</H4>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">Add the following to your .NET config file</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">&lt;runtime&gt;</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">&lt;AppContextSwitchOverrides value=\"Switch.System.Net.DontEnableSchUseStrongCrypto=false\" /&gt;</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">&lt;/runtime&gt;</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">&nbsp;</P>\n<H4 style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">Method 3 (Hardcoded in the application)-</H4>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">Use this line of C# code in your application during the initialization so that all web calls will use the newer TLS 1.2 protocol-</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<LI-CODE lang=\"csharp\">System.Net.ServicePointManager.SecurityProtocol = SecurityProtocolType.Tls12;</LI-CODE>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">&nbsp;</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">If you are using PowerShell you can use the same object with this-</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<LI-CODE lang=\"powershell\">[System.Net.ServicePointManager]::SecurityProtocol = \"Tls12\"</LI-CODE>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">&nbsp;</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">More on these here-</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\"><A href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/dotnet/framework/network-programming/tls\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/dotnet/framework/network-programming/tls</A></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<H3>Browser Support&nbsp;(Edge/Chrome/Edge legacy/IE/Firefox/Safari)</H3>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">The following clients are known to be unable to use TLS 1.2. Update these clients to ensure uninterrupted access to the service.</P>\n<P style=\"margin: 0in; font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">&nbsp;</P>\n<UL style=\"margin-left: .375in; direction: ltr; unicode-bidi: embed; margin-top: 0in; margin-bottom: 0in;\" type=\"disc\">\n<LI style=\"margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; vertical-align: middle;\"><SPAN style=\"font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">Android 4.3 and earlier versions</SPAN></LI>\n<LI style=\"margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; vertical-align: middle;\"><SPAN style=\"font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">Firefox version 5.0 and earlier versions</SPAN></LI>\n<LI style=\"margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; rel=\"noopener\">https://docs.microsoft.com/en-gb/archive/blogs/spses/cloud-search-service-application-removing-items-from-the-office-365-search-index</A>&nbsp;, it had the script to perform the same.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>However, the end user had their accounts configured with Multi Factor Authentication and the above didn't have the context.<BR /><BR />Went ahead and tweaked the script I came across an issue of using REST API <EM>ValidateUpdateListItem()</EM> to update listitem metadata. There’re a few blogs published on method <EM>ValidateUpdateListItem()</EM> for <EM>SharePoint Online</EM>. A few benefits of using <EM>ValidateUpdateListItem</EM> are:</P>\n<UL>\n<LI>Update list items without increasing its item version (see <A href=\"https://www.c-sharpcorner.com/article/update-a-sharepoint-list-item-without-increasing-its-item-file-version-using-res/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">this blog</A> for details).</LI>\n<LI>Easier to update some types of metadata, like Taxonomy, People and Lookup fields (mentioned in <A href=\"https://robertschouten.com/2018/04/30/update-file-metadata-with-rest-api-using-validateupdatelistitem-method/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Robert's blog</A>).</LI>\n</UL>\n<P>Besides <A href=\"https://robertschouten.com/2018/04/30/update-file-metadata-with-rest-api-using-validateupdatelistitem-method/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Robert's blog</A>, <A href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/pulse/list-items-system-update-options-sharepoint-online-andrew-koltyakov/?src=aff-lilpar&amp;veh=aff_src.aff-lilpar_c.partners_pkw.10078_plc.Skimbit%20Ltd._pcrid.449670_learning&amp;trk=aff_src.aff-lilpar_c.partners_pkw.10078_plc.Skimbit%20Ltd._pcrid.449670_learning&amp;clickid=2133FhSjJxyJRNEwUx0Mo34lUkizG9V1py1kUg0&amp;irgwc=1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Andrew’s blog</A> also presented detailed info about how to set various types of fields with <EM>ValidateUpdateListItem().</EM></P>\n<P>My issue was to update <STRONG>Editor</STRONG> and <STRONG>Author</STRONG> fields for a listitem on SharePoint on-premises (SP2016 and SP 2019) without increasing item version.</P>\n<P>Both <STRONG>Editor</STRONG> and <STRONG>Author</STRONG> are People and Group (Person) field. According above blogs, you can set the Person field, like:</P>\n<P>\"[{'Key':<STRONG>'</STRONG><STRONG>i:0#.f|membership</STRONG>|aaron@<SPAN>contoso.onmicrosoft.com</SPAN>'}]\"</P>\n<P>This works fine with SharePoint Online users. However, it does not work with SharePoint on-premises users, although no error returned from the method.</P>\n<P>After some testing, I found that for SharePoint on-premises users, you need to set the Persons field like below:</P>\n<P>\"[{'Key':'<STRONG>i:0#.w</STRONG>|aaron@testdomain.com'}]\"</P>\n<P>The sample below updates the <STRONG>Editor</STRONG> and <STRONG>Author</STRONG> fields on SharePoint on-premises (SP2016 and SP2019) without increasing item version.</P>\n<P>{</P>\n<P>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; \"formValues\": [</P>\n<P>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; {</P>\n<P>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; \"__metadata\": { \"type\": \"SP.ListItemFormUpdateValue\" },</P>\n<P>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; \"FieldName\": \"Editor\",</P>\n<P>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; \"FieldValue\": \"[{'Key':'i:0#.w|aaron@testdomain.com'}]\"</P>\n<P>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; },</P>\n<P>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; {</P>\n<P>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; \"__metadata\": { \"type\": \"SP.ListItemFormUpdateValue\" },</P>\n<P>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; \"FieldName\": \"Author\",</P>\n<P>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; \"FieldValue\": \"[{'Key':'i:0#.w|aaron@testdomain.com'}]\"</P>\n<P>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; }</P>\n<P>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; ],</P>\n<P>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; \"bNewDocumentUpdate\": true</P>\n<P>}</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>The REST API <EM>ValidateUpdateListItem()</EM> on the ListItem object is much easier in providing the Person field values to update. In addition, it has an option bNewDocumentUpdate to specify how you want item version to be updated.</P>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Thu, 27 Aug 2020 22:39:22 With the correlation IDs we can locate relevant errors in SharePoint ULS logs efficiently.<BR /><BR />However, not all failed requests expose the correlation ID to UI, code or through network traces. In those scenarios, being able to set distinctive correlation IDs when send the requests to SharePoint become very useful.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<OL>\n<LI><STRONG>For CSOM (</STRONG><STRONG>client object model code), it is straight forward to set it:</STRONG></LI>\n</OL>\n<P><BR /><EM>ClientContext context = </EM><EM>new</EM><EM> ClientContext(</EM><EM>\"https://{site_url}\"</EM><EM>);<BR />Web web = context.Web;</EM></P>\n<P><STRONG><EM>context.TraceCorrelationId = \"88888888111111112222222233333333\";</EM></STRONG></P>\n<P><EM>context.Load(web);</EM></P>\n<P><EM>context.ExecuteQuery();<BR /><BR /></EM></P>\n<OL start=\"2\">\n<LI><STRONG>For JSOM (JavaScript library code):<BR /><BR /></STRONG></LI>\n</OL>\n<P><EM>&lt;script type=\"text/javascript\"&gt; margin-bottom: 0; vertical-align: middle; color: #002060;\"><SPAN style=\"font-family: Calibri; font-size: 11.0pt;\">Test 2013 workflow</SPAN></LI>\n</OL>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Thu, 27 Aug 2020 22:48:29 +0000","feedId":13333,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"8990e7da5a859ad2fc558de145ad0975","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"Premkumarkc","publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295794918},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:49:54","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:49:54","title":"SharePoint / Script to locate documents encrypted with passwords","link":"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/microsoft-sharepoint-blog/sharepoint-script-to-locate-documents-encrypted-with-passwords/ba-p/1512775","description":"<H2>Summary</H2>\n<P>A customer asked if there was a method to identity documents stored in SharePoint online that were encrypted with passwords. Since nothing like this existed, it was created using PowerShell. I’m sharing this because the logic in the script may be useful for others.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<H2>The Code</H2>\n<PRE class=\"powershell\">#Title: find-docpasswords<BR />#Description: Iterates through each item in a specified list to find documents stored with passwords.<BR />#Date: 7/8/2020<BR />#Author: Mike Lee<BR />#Disclaimer: This PowerShell script is provided \"as-is\" with no warranties expressed or implied. Use it at your own risk.<BR />#Dependencies: SharePoint Online Client Components SDK: https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/download/details.aspx?id=42038<BR />#Tested with SharePoint Online Client Components SDK version 16.0.6906.1200<BR />#Parameters: $SiteURL, $ListName, $username<BR /><BR /><BR />#Add references to SharePoint client assemblies<BR />[System.Reflection.Assembly]::LoadWithPartialName(\"Microsoft.SharePoint.Client\")<BR />[System.Reflection.Assembly]::LoadWithPartialName(\"WindowsBase\")<BR /><BR /><BR />#Your SPO Tenant<BR />$SiteURL = \"https://tenant.sharepoint.com\"<BR /><BR />#The name of your document library<BR />$Listname = \"Documents\"<BR /><BR />#The admin account that has access to the library<BR />$username = \"admin@tenant.onmicrosoft.com\"<BR />$password = Read-Host \"Enter Password\" -AsSecureString<BR /><BR />#Building Context<BR />$ctx = New-Object Microsoft.SharePoint.Client.ClientContext($SiteURL)<BR />$ctx.Credentials = New-Object Microsoft.SharePoint.Client.SharePointOnlineCredentials($userName, $password)<BR />$List = $ctx.Web.Lists.GetByTitle($ListName) <BR /><BR /><BR />#CAML Query to recursively look at all items in the library with a 5000 item row limit. <BR />$camlQuery = New-Object Microsoft.SharePoint.Client.CamlQuery<BR />$camlQuery.ViewXml = @\"<BR />&lt;View Scope=\"RecursiveAll\"&gt;<BR />&lt;Query&gt;<BR />&lt;OrderBy&gt;&lt;FieldRef Name='ID' Ascending='TRUE'/&gt;&lt;/OrderBy&gt;<BR />&lt;/Query&gt;<BR />&lt;RowLimit Paged=\"TRUE\"&gt;5000&lt;/RowLimit&gt;<BR />&lt;/View&gt;<BR />\"@<BR /><BR />$items = $list.GetItems($camlQuery)<BR />$ctx.Load($items)<BR />$ctx.ExecuteQuery()<BR /><BR />#function to read documents<BR /><BR />function find-docpasswords($ctx, $FileUrl)<BR />{<BR />#Collect Documents Data<BR />$FileURL = $Item.FieldValues['FileRef']<BR /><BR />#Read the files from SharePoint online document library.<BR />$fileInfo = [Microsoft.SharePoint.Client.File]::OpenBinaryDirect($ctx,$FileURL)<BR />$stream = New-Object System.IO.MemoryStream<BR />$fileInfo.Stream.CopyTo($stream)<BR /><BR />#Read the first row of bytes as text<BR />$Start = [System.Text.Encoding]::Default.GetString($stream.ToArray()[0000..2000])<BR /><BR /># Record files that are password protected<BR />if($Start -match \"E.n.c.r.y.p.t.e.d.P.a.c.k.a.g.e\")<BR />{<BR />Write-Host \"$SiteURL$FileURL -- Is Password Protected\" -ForegroundColor Yellow<BR />}<BR />else<BR />{<BR />Write-Host \"$SiteURL$FileURL -- Not Password Protected\" -ForegroundColor Green<BR />}<BR /><BR />$stream.Close()<BR />$fileinfo.Dispose()<BR />$ctx.Dispose()<BR />}<BR /><BR /><BR />#Run the function to loop through all items in the library and find documents stored with passwords<BR /><BR />foreach($item in $items)<BR />{<BR />$fileUrl = $item.FieldValues[\"fileref\"]<BR />find-docpasswords $ctx $fileurl<BR />}</PRE>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<H2>Takeaways</H2>\n<P>This scripts loops though a specified document library and reads the first 200 binary bytes as text. If the encrypted string is found, the document URL is reported in the console output.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Here is an example of the output:</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-inline\" image-alt=\"4.png\" style=\"width: 982px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/204451i82223FEFF93CFA99/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"4.png\" alt=\"4.png\" /></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>You will need a few things to make this works.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<OL type=\"1\">\n<LI>Installed the<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN><A href=\"https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/download/details.aspx?id=42038\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">SharePoint Online Client Components SDK</A></LI>\n</OL>\n<OL start=\"2\" type=\"1\">\n<LI>Specify the “$SiteURL, $Listname, and $username in the script.</LI>\n</OL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Tue, 01 Sep 2020 19:55:34 +0000","feedId":13333,"bgimg":"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/204451i82223FEFF93CFA99/image-size/large?v=1.0&px=999","linkMd5":"345859e562804e94e5042db0a125bbad","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn60@2020_3/2020/09/05/08-49-55-575_57d7d867141c1dfc.webp","destWidth":982,"destHeight":126,"sourceBytes":33588,"destBytes":35116,"author":"Mike Lee (BOSTON)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/204451i82223FEFF93CFA99/image-size/large?v=1.0&px=999":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn60@2020_3/2020/09/05/08-49-55-575_57d7d867141c1dfc.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295794892},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:49:54","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:49:54","title":"SharePoint - SSL Offloading","link":"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/microsoft-sharepoint-blog/sharepoint-ssl-offloading/ba-p/1197236","description":"<P><STRONG>Contents</STRONG></P>\n<UL>\n<LI><FONT size=\"3\"><STRONG> What is SSL Offloading</STRONG></FONT></LI>\n<LI><FONT size=\"3\"><STRONG>Configuring SSL Offloading with SharePoint</STRONG></FONT>\n<UL>\n<LI><FONT size=\"3\">Web Applications</FONT></LI>\n<LI><FONT size=\"3\">Host Names Site Collections</FONT></LI>\n<LI><FONT size=\"3\">SharePoint Apps (App Domain</FONT></LI>\n</UL>\n</LI>\n<LI><FONT size=\"3\"><STRONG>Common Issues</STRONG></FONT>\n<UL>\n<LI><FONT size=\"3\">URLs returned to users are incorrect</FONT></LI>\n<LI><FONT size=\"3\">List or library Dropdown menu not loading</FONT></LI>\n<LI><FONT size=\"3\">After configuring SSL offloading for a web application users receive a 404 or 503</FONT></LI>\n</UL>\n</LI>\n<LI><FONT size=\"3\"><STRONG>Additional Information</STRONG></FONT>\n<UL>\n<LI><FONT size=\"3\">Creating IIS bindings for SharePoint Web Applications through PowerShell</FONT></LI>\n</UL>\n</LI>\n</UL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>What is SSL Offloading?</STRONG></P>\n<P>The idea behind SSL offloading is to reduce the load on web servers as well as the administrative overhead of managing SSL certificates across multiple servers. This is accomplished by using a dedicated network device (often times a network load balancer or a proxy server) to terminate SSL as it routes the requests. This removes the burden of decrypting and encrypting https traffic from the web server as well as providing a single location to host the SSL certificate reducing administrative efforts of maintaining and replacing certificates.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>What it looks like:</STRONG></P>\n<DIV id=\"tinyMceEditorPamBarber_0\" class=\"mceNonEditable lia-copypaste-placeholder\">&nbsp;</DIV>\n<DIV id=\"tinyMceEditorPamBarber_1\" class=\"mceNonEditable lia-copypaste-placeholder\">&nbsp;</DIV>\n<P><span class=\"lia-inline-image-display-wrapper lia-image-align-center\" image-alt=\"whatssllooks.png\" style=\"width: 999px;\"><img src=\"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/image/serverpage/image-id/173712i47FFB26A3403B3BF/image-size/large?v=1.0&amp;px=999\" title=\"whatssllooks.png\" alt=\"SharePoint SSL Offloading Request\" /><span class=\"lia-inline-image-caption\" onclick=\"event.preventDefault();\">SharePoint SSL Offloading Request</span></span></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<OL>\n<LI>The user makes an https request for a webpage that is routed to the load balancer</LI>\n<LI>The load balancer terminates SSL and sends the unencrypted http request to the web server</LI>\n<LI>The Web server handles the request and returns an unencrypted http response to the load balancer</LI>\n<LI>The load balancer encrypts the request and forwards it to the client that made the original request as https</LI>\n</OL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Configuring SSL Offloading with SharePoint</STRONG></P>\n<P><STRONG>Web Applications</STRONG></P>\n<P>To configure a SharePoint web application to take advantage of SSL offloading the Alternate Access Mappings must be configured in a specific way that allows the request to be accepted as http but have links rendered as https. By using internal URLs we can tell SharePoint to recognize an incoming request to http://sharepoint and handle it as though it were https:/sharepoint. Below illustrates how Alternate Access Mappings should be configured to allow for SSL offloading to occur. Note that the internal URL should match the traffic between the load balancer and SharePoint while the public url should reflect what URL users think they are using.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>If you are creating a new web application to be used with SSL offloading use the below settings as a guide to create it.</P>\n<TABLE>\n<TBODY>\n<TR>\n<TD>\n<P>Host Header</P>\n</TD>\n<TD>\n<P><A href=\"http://www.contoso.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">www.contoso.com</A></P>\n</TD>\n</TR>\n<TR>\n<TD>\n<P>Port</P>\n</TD>\n<TD>\n<P>80</P>\n</TD>\n</TR>\n<TR>\n<TD>\n<P>User Secure Sockets Layer (SSL)</P>\n</TD>\n<TD>\n<P>No</P>\n</TD>\n</TR>\n<TR>\n<TD>\n<P>Public Url</P>\n</TD>\n<TD>\n<P><A href=\"https://www.contoso.com:80\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://www.contoso.com:80</A></P>\n</TD>\n</TR>\n</TBODY>\n</TABLE>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>If you are configuring an existing HTTPS Web Application for SSL offloading add an internal URL using the same hostname over http to the zone they wish to use SSL offloading with. The end result should look like the example below. To add these you will want to go to <STRONG>Central Administration &gt; Application Management &gt; Configure Alternate Access Mappings &gt; Add Internal URLs</STRONG>.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<TABLE>\n<TBODY>\n<TR>\n<TD>\n<P><STRONG>Zone </STRONG></P>\n</TD>\n<TD>\n<P><STRONG>Internal Url </STRONG></P>\n</TD>\n<TD>\n<P><STRONG>Public Url </STRONG></P>\n</TD>\n</TR>\n<TR>\n<TD rowspan=\"2\">\n<P>Default</P>\n</TD>\n<TD>\n<P>https://sharepoint</P>\n</TD>\n<TD>\n<P>https://sharepoint</P>\n</TD>\n</TR>\n<TR>\n<TD>\n<P>http://sharepoint</P>\n</TD>\n<TD>\n<P>https://sharepoint</P>\n</TD>\n</TR>\n</TBODY>\n</TABLE>\n<P><STRONG>&nbsp;</STRONG></P>\n<P><STRONG>Host Names Site Collections</STRONG></P>\n<P>In path based sites we can utilize a combination of internal and public URLs in the web app's AAMs to achieve the redirection that we need. While we do have multiple <EM>zones</EM> for HNSCs we do not have the same functionality that internal and public URLs provide. As such the configuration for HNSCs is different as described below.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Web Application Configuration</STRONG></P>\n<UL>\n<LI>The web application should be configured the same way as seen above except the host header should remain empty</LI>\n<LI>HNSC should be created using an <STRONG>https</STRONG> URL</LI>\n</UL>\n<P>Example:</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<PRE>New-SPSite '<A href=\"https://portal.fabrikam.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://portal.fabrikam.com</A>' -HostHeaderWebApplication '<A href=\"https://sharepoint.contoso.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://sharepoint.contoso.com</A>' -Name 'Portal' -OwnerAlias 'contoso\\administrator' -Language 1033 -Template 'STS#0'</PRE>\n<UL>\n<LI>Bindings for the backing IIS site should include an <STRONG>http</STRONG> binding with a blank host-header if not already present</LI>\n</UL>\n<P><STRONG>Proxy or Load Balancer Configuration</STRONG></P>\n<P>Since we cannot use internal URLs like we would for a path based site collections we must configure the proxy server or load balancer that is serving as the point of SSL/TLS termination to add an additional header to the web requests. The header <EM>Front-End-Https</EM> tells SharePoint whether the links that it renders for this web request should be rendered as http or https.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<TABLE>\n<THEAD>\n<TR>\n<TD colspan=\"2\">\n<P>Front-End-Https</P>\n</TD>\n</TR>\n<TR>\n<TD>\n<P><STRONG>Value</STRONG></P>\n</TD>\n<TD>\n<P><STRONG>Description</STRONG></P>\n</TD>\n</TR>\n</THEAD>\n<TBODY>\n<TR>\n<TD>\n<P>On</P>\n</TD>\n<TD>\n<P>The request made by the <STRONG>end user</STRONG> was made over <STRONG>https</STRONG></P>\n<P>Example: <STRONG>Front-End-Https: On</STRONG></P>\n</TD>\n</TR>\n<TR>\n<TD>\n<P>Off</P>\n</TD>\n<TD>\n<P>The request made by the <STRONG>end user</STRONG> was made over <STRONG>http</STRONG></P>\n</TD>\n</TR>\n</TBODY>\n</TABLE>\n<P><EM>&nbsp;</EM></P>\n<P><EM>Public Content: <A href=\"https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/cc424952(v%3Doffice.15).aspx#section2g\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Use host-named site collections with off-box SSL termination</A> </EM></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>SharePoint Apps (App Domain)</STRONG></P>\n<P>When attempting to configure SSL offloading for app domains you may see the below error:</P>\n<P>03/05/2015 09:13:34.20 w3wp.exe (0x0XXX) 0x0XXX SharePoint Foundation General aiz2a High Request for app scheme does not match the webapp's scheme for this zone. Request Uri: <A href=\"http://app-XXXXXXXXX.apps.contoso.com…\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">http://app-XXXXXXXXX.apps.contoso.com…</A>. Zone Response Uri: <A href=\"https://sharepoint.contoso.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://sharepoint.contoso.com</A> Site collection path: /</P>\n<P>To allow requests between web applications and app domains to be handled under different protocol schemes (http and https) as you would see when configuring SSL offloading for both web apps and app domains run the below PowerShell to enable support for multiple app domains.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<LI-CODE lang=\"markup\">   $contentService = [Microsoft.SharePoint.Administration.SPWebService]::ContentService\n   $contentService.SupportMultipleAppDomains = $true\n   $contentService.Update()</LI-CODE>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><EM>Public Content: <A href=\"https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/fp161236.aspx\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Configure an environment for apps for SharePoint (SharePoint 2013)</A> </EM></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Common Issues</STRONG></P>\n<P><STRONG>URLs returned to users are incorrect</STRONG></P>\n<P>When an environment with SSL offloading is not configured correctly it is not uncommon to see the URL in link rendered by SharePoint such as navigation to be incorrect. I.e. all links are rendered in http instead of https or in some scenarios even a different host name. This is most commonly caused by the configuration of alternate access mappings.</P>\n<P>Document the following:</P>\n<OL>\n<LI>The address and protocol that the users utilize to access the site.</LI>\n<LI>The address and protocol that the load balancer (or point of SSL termination) forwards the request as. It is possible that the hostname could differ as well as the protocol.</LI>\n</OL>\n<P>With the answers to the above ensure that the alternate access mappings for the web application are configured as seen below where the numbers coordinate to the responses from the above:</P>\n<OL>\n<LI>Public url matches url that users utilize.</LI>\n<LI>Internal url matches url of incoming requests from the load balancer, if it is not present click <EM>Add Internal URLs</EM> on the <EM>Configure Alternate Access Mappings</EM> page in Central Administration.</LI>\n</OL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>List or library Dropdown menu not loading</STRONG></P>\n<P>This can be a problem when the site is accessed via Azure Application Proxy. See <A href=\"https://internal.support.services.microsoft.com/en-us/help/4459184\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https://internal.support.services.microsoft.com/en-us/help/4459184</A></P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>After configuring SSL offloading for a web application users receive a 404 or 503</STRONG></P>\n<P>This most often is due to the bindings in IIS. Locate the IIS site behind this zone of the web application.</P>\n<P>To modify the bindings of an IIS website:</P>\n<UL>\n<LI>Open <STRONG>Internet Information Services (IIS) Manager</STRONG> from <STRONG>Start &gt; Administrative Tools</STRONG></LI>\n<LI>Expand the server name in the <STRONG>Connections</STRONG> pane</LI>\n<LI>Expand <STRONG>Sites</STRONG></LI>\n<LI>Right click on the site that should be serving the requests for the SharePoint Web Application in question</LI>\n<LI>Ensure that there is both an https as well as an http binding for the hostname that will be accessed as seen in the image below</LI>\n</UL>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><STRONG>Additional Information</STRONG></P>\n<P><STRONG>Creating IIS bindings for SharePoint Web Applications through PowerShell</STRONG></P>\n<P>While you can add bindings to the SPWebApplication.IisSettings.ServerBindings array through PowerShell do note that this does <STRONG>not</STRONG> propagate to the existing IIS sites. This will however create the bindings when the <EM>SharePoint Foundation Web Application</EM> service is started on a server. As such any new server added to the farm, or any server where the web application service is started/restarted the bindings added through the below method will be reflected.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<LI-CODE lang=\"markup\"> \n   Add-PSSnapin Microsoft.SharePoint.PowerShell\n   $wa = Get-SPWebApplication 'http://sharepoint.contoso.com'\n   $binding = New-Object Microsoft.SharePoint.Administration.SPServerBinding\n   $binding.Port = 80\n   $binding.HostHeader = \"\"\n   #Note the \"Default\" below references the zone of the web application, if you wish to add a binding to a different zone replace that with the appropriate zone (Default/Intranet/Internet/Extranet/Custom).\n   $iis = $wa.IisSettings[\"Default\"]\n   $iis.ServerBindings.Add($binding)\n   $wa.Update()\n   #Call the provision method to push this out to all servers, note that this will overwrite any manual modifications to the web.config or other manual changes within IIS for this web app.\n   $wa.ProvisionGlobally()</LI-CODE>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P><EM>Special thanks to the original author: Ian Ragusa (Microsoft This tool has been deprecated but there is still a need to collect performance data for those pesky performance issues.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>The Perfwiz tool simply used LOGMAN.exe to create a custom counter set with several selected counters specifically for SharePoint servers.</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>This blog will detail how to use LOGMAN.exe to mimic the baseline counter set that was created by the Perfwiz tool.</P>\n<H2>&nbsp;</H2>\n<H2>The command Line</H2>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Here is the command used to create the Baseline counter set:</P>\n<P>&nbsp;</P>\n<P>Logman.exe create
